10124-8{_}892{_}But of course it never amounted to anything until the railroad was built."
10124-8{_}893{_}Next day they were sitting in a group before the hotel when a man was seen approaching them with shuffling steps.
10124-8{_}894{_}Uncle John looked at him closely and Mumbles leaped from Patsy's lap and rushed at the stranger with excited barks.
10124-8{_}895{_}"Why, it's Wampus," said Mr. Merrick.
10124-8{_}896{_}"The car must have arrived."
10124-8{_}897{_}Wampus caught up the baby dog and held it under his arm while he took his cap off and bowed respectfully to his employer.
10124-8{_}898{_}"He an' me, we here," he announced.
10124-8{_}899{_}"Who is 'he,' Wampus?"
10124-8{_}900{_}"Aut'mob'l'."
10124-8{_}901{_}"When did you arrive?"
10124-8{_}902{_}"Half hour ago.
10124-8{_}903{_}He on side track."
10124-8{_}904{_}"Very good.
10124-8{_}905{_}You have made capital time, for a freight train.
10124-8{_}906{_}Let us go at once and get the car unloaded."
10124-8{_}907{_}Wampus hesitated, looking sheepish.
10124-8{_}908{_}"I been arrest," he said.
10124-8{_}909{_}"Arrested!
10124-8{_}910{_}For what?"
10124-8{_}911{_}"I make speed.
10124-8{_}912{_}They not like it.
10124-8{_}913{_}They arrest me--_Me_--Wampus!"
10124-8{_}914{_}He straightened his slim little form with an assumption of dignity.
10124-8{_}915{_}"I knew it," sighed the Major.
10124-8{_}916{_}"I decided he was a speed fiend the first time I saw him."
10124-8{_}917{_}"But--dear me!"
10124-8{_}918{_}said Uncle John; "how could you be arrested for speeding when the automobile was on a fiat car?"
10124-8{_}919{_}Wampus glanced over his shoulder.
10124-8{_}920{_}Two railroad men had followed him and were now lounging against the porch railing.
10124-8{_}921{_}One had his right eye bandaged while the other carried one arm in a sling.
10124-8{_}922{_}Both scowled as they eyed the Canadian fixedly.
10124-8{_}923{_}"Freight train make pretty slow time," began the chauffeur.
10124-8{_}924{_}"I know you in hurry, so freight train he make me nervous.
10124-8{_}925{_}I say polite to conductor I like to go faster.
10124-8{_}926{_}He laugh.
10124-8{_}927{_}I say polite to brakeman we must go faster.
10124-8{_}928{_}He make abusing speech.
10124-8{_}929{_}I climb into engine an' say polite to engineer to turn on steam.
10124-8{_}930{_}He insult me.
10124-8{_}931{_}So I put my foot on him an' run engine myself.
10124-8{_}932{_}I am Wampus.
10124-8{_}933{_}I understan' engine--all kinds.
10124-8{_}934{_}Brakeman he swear; he swear so bad I put him off train.
10124-8{_}935{_}Conductor must have lump of coal in eye to keep quiet.
10124-8{_}936{_}Fireman he jus' smile an' whistle soft an' say nothing; so we friends.
10124-8{_}937{_}When I say 'shovel in coal,' he shovel.
10124-8{_}938{_}When we pass stations quick like, he whistle with engine loud.
10124-8{_}939{_}So now we here an' I been arrest."
10124-8{_}940{_}Patsy tittered and stuffed her handkerchief into her mouth.
10124-8{_}941{_}Uncle John first chuckled and then looked grave.
10124-8{_}942{_}The Major advanced to Wampus and soberly shook his hand.
10124-8{_}943{_}"You're a brave man, sir, for a chauffeur," he said.
10124-8{_}944{_}"I congratulate you,"  Wampus still looked uneasy.
10124-8{_}945{_}"I been arrest," he repeated.
10124-8{_}946{_}Uncle John beckoned the railroad men to come forward.
10124-8{_}947{_}"Is this story true?"
10124-8{_}948{_}he asked.
10124-8{_}949{_}"Most of it, sir," answered the conductor.
10124-8{_}950{_}"It's only by the mercy of Providence we're here alive.
10124-8{_}951{_}This scoundrel held up the whole crew and ran away with the engine.
10124-8{_}952{_}We might have had a dozen collisions or smash-ups, for he went around curves at sixty miles an hour.
10124-8{_}953{_}We'd cut our train in two, so as to pull half of it at a time up the grade at Lamy, and so there were only six cars on this end of it.
10124-8{_}954{_}The other half is seventy miles back, and part of what we have here ought to have been left at the way stations.
10124-8{_}955{_}I can't make out, sir, whether it's burglary, or highway robbery or arson an' murder he's guilty of, or all of 'em; but I've telegraphed for instructions and I'll hold him a prisoner until the superintendent tells me what to do with him."
10124-8{_}956{_}Mr. Merrick was very sober now.
10124-8{_}957{_}"The matter is serious," he said.
10124-8{_}958{_}"This man is in my employ, but I did not hire him to steal a railway train or fight its crew.
10124-8{_}959{_}Not badly hurt, I hope, sir?"
10124-8{_}960{_}"My eye's pretty bad," growled the conductor.
10124-8{_}961{_}"Tom, here, thought his arm was broken, at first; but I guess it's only sprained."
10124-8{_}962{_}"How about the brakeman he threw off the train?"
10124-8{_}963{_}"Why, we were not going fast, just then, and it didn't hurt him.
10124-8{_}964{_}We saw him get up and shake his fist at the robber.
10124-8{_}965{_}If he ever meets Mr. Wampus again he'll murder him."
10124-8{_}966{_}"Come with me to the telegraph office and I'll see what I can do to straighten this out," said Mr. Merrick briskly.
10124-8{_}967{_}On the way he remarked to the conductor: "I'm sorry I let Wampus travel alone.
10124-8{_}968{_}He's just a little bit affected in his mind, you know, and at times isn't responsible for what he does."
10124-8{_}969{_}The conductor scratched his head doubtfully.
10124-8{_}970{_}"I suspected he was crazy," he replied, "and that's why I didn't hurt him.
10124-8{_}971{_}But if he's crazy he's the most deliberate loonatic I ever run acrost."
10124-8{_}972{_}The superintendent had just wired instructions to put the outlaw in jail when Mr. Merrick reached the telegraph office, but after an hour spent in sending messages back and forth a compromise was affected and the little millionaire had agreed to pay a goodly sum to the company by way of damages and to satisfy the crew of the freight train--which he succeeded in doing by a further outlay of money.
10124-8{_}973{_}"You're not worth all this bother," said Mr. Merrick to the humbled Wampus, when the final settlement had been made, "but chauffeurs are scarce in Albuquerque and I can't be delayed.
10124-8{_}974{_}Never, sir, while you are in my employ, must you allow yourself to be guilty of such an act again!"
10124-8{_}975{_}Wampus sighed.
10124-8{_}976{_}"Never," he promised, "will I ride by freight train again.
10124-8{_}977{_}Send car by express.
10124-8{_}978{_}I am Wampus.
10124-8{_}979{_}Freight train he make me nervous."
10124-8{_}980{_}The automobile was quickly unloaded and at once Wampus set to work to get it in running order.
10124-8{_}981{_}He drove it to the hotel at about sundown and Mr. Merrick told the girls to be ready to start after an early breakfast the next morning.
10124-8{_}982{_}"Which way do we go?"
10124-8{_}983{_}asked the Major.
10124-8{_}984{_}"We'll have a talk with Wampus this evening and decide," said Uncle John.
10124-8{_}985{_}"Don't leave out the Grand Canyon!"
10124-8{_}986{_}begged Patsy.
10124-8{_}987{_}"Nor the Petrified Forests."
10124-8{_}988{_}added Beth.
10124-8{_}989{_}"And couldn't we visit the Moki Indian reservation?"
10124-8{_}990{_}"Those things may be well enough in their way," observed the Major, "but is their way our way?
10124-8{_}991{_}That's the question.
10124-8{_}992{_}The one thing we must take into consideration is the matter of roads.
10124-8{_}993{_}We must discover which road is the best and then take it.
10124-8{_}994{_}We're not out of the mountains yet, and we shall have left the railroad, the last vestige of civilization, behind us."
10124-8{_}995{_}But the conference evolved the fact, according to Wampus, that the best and safest roads were for a time along the line of the Santa Fe, directly west; and this would enable them to visit most of the scenes the girls were eager to see.
10124-8{_}996{_}"No boulevard in mountain anywhere," remarked Wampus; "but road he good enough to ride on.
10124-8{_}997{_}Go slow an' go safe.
10124-8{_}998{_}I drive 'Autocrat' from here to Los Angeles blindfold."
10124-8{_}999{_}With this assurance they were obliged to be content, and an eager and joyful party assembled next morning to begin the journey so long looked forward to.
10124-8{_}1000{_}The landlord of the hotel, a man with a careworn face, shook his head dismally and predicted their return to Albuquerque within twenty-four hours.
10124-8{_}1001{_}"Of course people _do_ make the trip from here to the coast," he said; "but it's mighty seldom, and they all swear they'll never do it again.
10124-8{_}1002{_}It's uncomfortable, and it's dangerous."
10124-8{_}1003{_}"Why?"
10124-8{_}1004{_}asked Uncle John.
10124-8{_}1005{_}"You're headed through a wild country, settled only by Mexicans, Indians, and gangs of cowboys still worse.
10124-8{_}1006{_}The roads are something awful.
10124-8{_}1007{_}That man Wampus is an optimist, and will tackle anything and then be sorry for it afterward.
10124-8{_}1008{_}The towns are scattered from here on, and you won't strike a decent meal except at the railway stations.
10124-8{_}1009{_}Taking all these things into consideration, I advise you to make your headquarters here for the winter."
10124-8{_}1010{_}"Thank you," returned Mr. Merrick pleasantly.
10124-8{_}1011{_}"It's too late for us to back out now, even if we felt nervous and afraid, which I assure you we do not."
10124-8{_}1012{_}"We are not looking for excessive comfort on this journey, you know," remarked Patsy.
10124-8{_}1013{_}"But thank you for your warning, sir.
10124-8{_}1014{_}It has given us great pleasure; for if there were no chance of adventure before us we should all be greatly disappointed."
10124-8{_}1015{_}Again the landlord shook his head.
10124-8{_}1016{_}"Right?"
10124-8{_}1017{_}asked Wampus, at the wheel.
10124-8{_}1018{_}"Go ahead," said Mr. Merrick, and slowly the big car started upon its journey into the Golden West.
10124-8{_}1019{_}The air was keen and bracing, but not chilly.
10124-8{_}1020{_}The sunshine flooded the landscape on every side.
10124-8{_}1021{_}All the windows of the limousine had been lowered.
10124-8{_}1022{_}Myrtle Dean had been established in one corner of the broad back seat, where she nestled comfortably among the cushions.
10124-8{_}1023{_}Uncle John sat beside her, with Beth and the Major on the seat on front.
10124-8{_}1024{_}There were two folding chairs that could be used on occasion, and the back seat easily accommodated three, the "Autocrat" being a seven passenger car; but Patsy was perched in front beside Wampus, which was really the choicest seat of all, so there was ample room inside to "swing a cat," as the Major stated--if anyone had cared to attempt such a feat.
10124-8{_}1025{_}Of course the wee Mumbles was in Patsy's lap, and he seemed to have overcome his first aversion of Wampus and accepted the little chauffeur into the circle of his favored acquaintances.
10124-8{_}1026{_}Indeed, they soon became fast friends.
10124-8{_}1027{_}On leaving the town Wampus turned into a smooth, hard wagon road that ran in zigzag fashion near the railroad grade.
10124-8{_}1028{_}The car bowled along right merrily for some twenty miles, when the driver turned to the right and skimmed along a high plateau.
10124-8{_}1029{_}It was green and seemed fertile, but scarcely a farmhouse could they see, although the clear air permitted a broad view.
10124-8{_}1030{_}"He up hill now all way to Continental Divide," said Wampus to Patsy; "then he go down hill long time."
10124-8{_}1031{_}"It doesn't seem to be much uphill," returned the girl, "and the road is very good."
10124-8{_}1032{_}"We make time here," observed the driver.
10124-8{_}1033{_}"By'm-by we find rock an' bad road.
10124-8{_}1034{_}Then we go slow."
10124-8{_}1035{_}The Major was watching the new chauffeur carefully, and despite his dismal forebodings the man seemed not at all reckless but handled his car with rare skill.
10124-8{_}1036{_}So the critic turned to his brother-in-law and asked:  "Is it fully decided which way we shall go?"
10124-8{_}1037{_}"I've left it to Wampus and the girls," was the reply.
10124-8{_}1038{_}"On account of our little invalid here we shall take the most direct route to California.
10124-8{_}1039{_}It isn't a short route, at that.
10124-8{_}1040{_}On Beth's account we shall visit the Moki and Navajo reservations, and on Patsy's account we're going by way of the Grand Canyon of Arizona.
10124-8{_}1041{_}Wampus says he knows every inch of the road, so for my part I'm content to be just a passenger."
10124-8{_}1042{_}"Which remark," said the Major, "indicates that I'm to be just a passenger also.
10124-8{_}1043{_}Very well, John; I'm willing.
10124-8{_}1044{_}There may be trouble ahead of us, but to-day is so magnificent that it's wise to forget everything but the present."
10124-8{_}1045{_}CHAPTER VII  THE CHAUFFEUR IMPROVES   They all enjoyed that first day's ride.
10124-8{_}1046{_}Wampus did not drive fast, for there were places where he couldn't; yet by one o'clock they had reached Laguna, sixty miles from their starting point.
10124-8{_}1047{_}There was an excellent railway hotel here, so they decided to spend the rest of the day and the night at Laguna and proceed early the next morning.
10124-8{_}1048{_}The big car was an object of much curiosity to the natives, and during the afternoon Wampus was the center of attraction.
10124-8{_}1049{_}Myrtle had stood the ride remarkably well, and Uncle John noticed that her eyes were brighter and a shade of color had already crept into her pale cheeks.
10124-8{_}1050{_}Having risen early all three of the girls took a nap during the afternoon, as did Mr. Merrick.
10124-8{_}1051{_}The Major gossiped with the station agent, the most important individual in town, and gleaned sundry information that made him look rather glum.
10124-8{_}1052{_}"I don't say the road's exactly dangerous, mind you," added the man, "but these greasers and Injuns get mischievous, at times, harmless as they look.
10124-8{_}1053{_}All I'm advisin' is that you keep a sharp eye on 'em."
10124-8{_}1054{_}Finding Wampus cleaning his car, while a circle of silent, attentive inhabitants looked on, the Major said to him in a low voice: "Have you a revolver?"
10124-8{_}1055{_}Wampus shook his head.
10124-8{_}1056{_}"Never carry him," he replied.
10124-8{_}1057{_}"All gun he make trouble.
10124-8{_}1058{_}Sometime he shoot wrong man.
10124-8{_}1059{_}Don't like gun.
10124-8{_}1060{_}Why should I?
10124-8{_}1061{_}I am Wampus!"
10124-8{_}1062{_}The Major entered the hotel frowning.
10124-8{_}1063{_}"That fellow," he muttered, "is a natural-born coward, and we needn't expect help from him if trouble comes."
10124-8{_}1064{_}No trouble came that night, however, and in the early morning, while the sky was still reddened by the rising sun, they were off again, following more closely now the railroad, as rocky defiles began to loom up before them.
10124-8{_}1065{_}By the zigzag course they were obliged to take it was ninety miles to Gallup, and this they easily made, despite the growing steepness of the mountain road.
10124-8{_}1066{_}Here was the famous Continental Divide, and the State of Arizona lay just beyond.
10124-8{_}1067{_}The Continental Divide is the ridge that separates the streams tributary to the Atlantic ocean from those tributary to the Pacific, so that after crossing it one might well feel that at last the East was left behind and the great West with its romance now faced him.
10124-8{_}1068{_}They came to the little town in time to see the gorgeous sunset from this, the highest point of the Rockies, and especially to Myrtle, who had traveled so little, was the sight impressive and awe inspiring.
10124-8{_}1069{_}There was a small but fairly good hotel in the place, and after supper Patsy and Beth went out for a stroll, being much interested in the dark-skinned Mexicans and still darker Indians who constituted far the larger part of the population.
10124-8{_}1070{_}The party had everywhere met with respect from these people, who, although curious, were silent and well-behaved; so Uncle John and the Major, deep in a political argument on the hotel porch, had no thought of danger when they saw the two girls start away arm in arm.
10124-8{_}1071{_}The sky was still aglow, although the sun had set, and in the subdued light the coarse adobe huts and rickety frame dwellings were endowed with a picturesque appearance they did not really possess.
10124-8{_}1072{_}Beth and Patsy came to the end of the main street rather suddenly, and stood a moment looking at the shadows cast by the rocky cliffs near by.
10124-8{_}1073{_}Some of the peaks had snow upon them, and there was a chill in the air, now that the sun had withdrawn its warmth.
10124-8{_}1074{_}The girls turned presently and took another route that might bring them quicker to the hotel, but had only proceeded a short way when in passing a rather solitary adobe structure a man stepped from the shadow of the wall and confronted them.
10124-8{_}1075{_}He wore a red flannel shirt and a broad sombrero, the latter scarcely covering his dark, evil features.
10124-8{_}1076{_}The cousins stopped short.
10124-8{_}1077{_}Then Beth whispered: "Let's go the other way."
10124-8{_}1078{_}But as they were about to turn the Mexican drew a revolver and said in harsh, uneven English: "You halt.
10124-8{_}1079{_}Keep a-still, or I shoot."
10124-8{_}1080{_}"What do you want?"
10124-8{_}1081{_}asked Beth, quietly.
10124-8{_}1082{_}"Money.
10124-8{_}1083{_}All you got.
10124-8{_}1084{_}Jew'lry--all you got.
10124-8{_}1085{_}Give 'm quick, or I shoot!"
10124-8{_}1086{_}As they stood hesitating a sound of footsteps was heard and someone approached quickly from behind them.
10124-8{_}1087{_}Patsy looked hurriedly around and saw Wampus.
10124-8{_}1088{_}He was walking with his thin little form bent and his hands deep in his trousers pockets.
10124-8{_}1089{_}Incidentally Wampus was smoking the stub of a cigar, as was his custom when off duty.
10124-8{_}1090{_}The Mexican saw him, but marking his small size and mild manner did not flinch from his position.
10124-8{_}1091{_}With one revolver still leveled at the girls he drew another from a hip pocket and turned it upon Wampus.
10124-8{_}1092{_}"You stop--halt!"
10124-8{_}1093{_}he exclaimed fiercely.
10124-8{_}1094{_}Wampus did not halt.
10124-8{_}1095{_}His eyes fixed upon the bandit's ugly features, still puffing his cigar and with hands in his pockets he walked deliberately past Patsy and Beth and straight up to the muzzles of the revolvers.
10124-8{_}1096{_}"Stop!"
10124-8{_}1097{_}cried the Mexican; and again: "Stop!"
10124-8{_}1098{_}Wampus stopped when one revolver nearly touched his nose and another covered his body.
10124-8{_}1099{_}Slowly he drew one hand from his pocket and grasped the barrel of the nearest weapon.
10124-8{_}1100{_}"Let him go," he said, not raising his voice.
10124-8{_}1101{_}The man stared into the little chauffeur's eyes and released his hold of the revolver.
10124-8{_}1102{_}Wampus looked at it, grunted, and put it in his pocket.
10124-8{_}1103{_}"Now the other gun," he said.
10124-8{_}1104{_}The fellow drew back and half turned, as if to escape.
10124-8{_}1105{_}"No, no!"
10124-8{_}1106{_}said Wampus, as if annoyed.
10124-8{_}1107{_}"You give me gun.
10124-8{_}1108{_}See--I am Wampus!"
10124-8{_}1109{_}Sheepishly enough the Mexican surrendered the other weapon.
10124-8{_}1110{_}"Now turn aroun' an' go to hotel," commanded the chauffeur.
10124-8{_}1111{_}The man obeyed.
10124-8{_}1112{_}Wampus turned to the girls, who were now not only relieved but on the verge of laughter and said deprecatingly:  "Do not be scare, for poor man he make no harm.
10124-8{_}1113{_}He jus' try a goozle--no dare shoot here in town.
10124-8{_}1114{_}Then come; I go back with you."
10124-8{_}1115{_}Silently they accompanied him along the lane, the Mexican keeping in front and looking around from time to time to see if they followed.
10124-8{_}1116{_}A short distance from the hotel Wampus gave a queer whistle which brought the bandit cringing to his side.
10124-8{_}1117{_}Without ado he handed the fellow his two revolvers and said calmly: "Go 'long."
10124-8{_}1118{_}The Mexican "went along" briskly and the dusk soon swallowed him up.
10124-8{_}1119{_}"Thank you, Wampus," said Patsy, gratefully; "you've saved us from a dreadful experience."
10124-8{_}1120{_}"Oh, that!"
10124-8{_}1121{_}snapping his fingers scornfully.
10124-8{_}1122{_}"He not a good bad-man, for he too much afraid.
10124-8{_}1123{_}I have no gun, for I do not like gun.
10124-8{_}1124{_}Still, if I not come, he make you give him money an' trinkets."
10124-8{_}1125{_}"You were very kind," replied Beth, "and I thank you as much as Patsy does.
10124-8{_}1126{_}If you had not arrived just when you did I might have killed the man."
10124-8{_}1127{_}"You?"
10124-8{_}1128{_}inquired Wampus, doubtingly.
10124-8{_}1129{_}"Yes."
10124-8{_}1130{_}She showed him a small pearl-handled revolver which she carried in the pocket of her jacket.
10124-8{_}1131{_}"I can shoot, Wampus."
10124-8{_}1132{_}The little chauffeur grinned; then looked grave and shook his head.
10124-8{_}1133{_}"It make funny world, these day," said he.
10124-8{_}1134{_}"One time girl from city would scream to see a gun; now she carry him in pocket an' can shoot!
10124-8{_}1135{_}Ver' fine; ver' fine.
10124-8{_}1136{_}But I like me old style girl who make scream.
10124-8{_}1137{_}Then a man not feel foolish when he try protect her."
10124-8{_}1138{_}Patsy laughed merrily; but Beth saw he was offended and hastened to say:  "I am very grateful to you, Wampus, and I know you are a brave and true man.
10124-8{_}1139{_}I shall expect you to protect me at all times, for I really don't wish to shoot anyone, although I think it best to carry a revolver.
10124-8{_}1140{_}Always after this, before I am tempted to fire, I shall look to see if you are not near me."
10124-8{_}1141{_}"All right," he said more cheerfully.
10124-8{_}1142{_}"I am Wampus.
10124-8{_}1143{_}I will be there, Miss 'Lizbeth."
10124-8{_}1144{_}CHAPTER VIII  AMONG THE INDIANS   Little Myrtle grew brighter day by day.
10124-8{_}1145{_}She even grew merry and developed a fine sense of humor, showing new traits in her hitherto undeveloped character.
10124-8{_}1146{_}The girl never mentioned her injury nor admitted that she suffered any pain, even when directly questioned.
10124-8{_}1147{_}Indeed she was not uncomfortable during that splendid automobile ride over mountain and plain into the paradise of the glowing West.
10124-8{_}1148{_}Never before in her life had Myrtle enjoyed an outing, except for an hour or two in a city park; never before had she known a friend to care for her and sympathize honestly with her griefs.
10124-8{_}1149{_}Therefore this experience was so exquisitely delightful that her responsive heart nearly burst with gratitude.
10124-8{_}1150{_}Pretty thoughts came to her that she had never had before; her luxurious surroundings led her to acquire dainty ways and a composed and self-poised demeanor.
10124-8{_}1151{_}"Our rosebud is unfolding, petal by petal, and beginning to bloom gloriously," said Patsy to sympathetic Uncle John.
10124-8{_}1152{_}"Could anyone be more sweet or lovely?"
10124-8{_}1153{_}Perhaps almost any girl, situated as Myrtle Dean was, would have blossomed under similar influences.
10124-8{_}1154{_}Certain it was that Uncle John came to have a tender affection for the poor child, while the Major's big heart had warmed from the first toward the injured girl.
10124-8{_}1155{_}Beth and Patsy were devoted to their new friend and even Mumbles was never so happy as when Myrtle would hold and caress him.
10124-8{_}1156{_}Naturally the former waif responded freely to all this wealth of affection and strove to be companionable and cheery, that they might forget as much as possible her physical helplessness.
10124-8{_}1157{_}Mumbles was not the least important member of the party, but proved a constant source of amusement to all.
10124-8{_}1158{_}In the novel domains they now traversed the small dog's excitable nature led him to investigate everything that seemed suspicious, but he was so cowardly, in spite of this, that once when Patsy let him down to chase a gopher or prairie dog--they were not sure which--the animal turned at bay and sent Mumbles retreating with his stubby tail between his legs.
10124-8{_}1159{_}His comradeship for Wampus surprised them all.
10124-8{_}1160{_}The Canadian would talk seriously to the dog and tell it long stories as if the creature could understand every word--which perhaps he did.
10124-8{_}1161{_}Mumbles would sit up between the driver and Patsy and listen attentively, which encouraged Wampus to talk until Patsy in self-defense turned and tossed the fuzzy animal in to Myrtle, who was always glad to receive him.
10124-8{_}1162{_}But Patsy did not always sit on the front seat.
10124-8{_}1163{_}That honor was divided among them all, by turns, except the Major, who did not care for the place.
10124-8{_}1164{_}Yet I think Patsy rode there oftener than anyone else, and it came to be considered her special privilege because she had first claimed it.
10124-8{_}1165{_}The Major, after the incident at Gallup, did not scorn Wampus so openly as before; but he still reserved a suspicion that the fellow was at heart a coward and a blusterer.
10124-8{_}1166{_}The chauffeur's sole demerit in the eyes of the others was his tremendous egotism.
10124-8{_}1167{_}The proud remark: "I am Wampus!"
10124-8{_}1168{_}was constantly on his lips and he had wonderful tales to tell to all who would listen of his past experiences, in every one of which he unblushingly figured as the hero.
10124-8{_}1169{_}But he really handled the big touring car in an admirable manner, and when one afternoon a tire was punctured by a cactus spine by the roadside--their first accident--they could not fail to admire the dexterous manner in which he changed the tube for a new one.
10124-8{_}1170{_}From Gallup they took a wagon road to Fort Defiance, in the Navajo Indian reservation; but the Navajos proved uninteresting people, not even occupying themselves in weaving the famous Navajo blankets, which are now mostly made in Philadelphia.
10124-8{_}1171{_}Even Patsy, who had longed to "see the Indians in their native haunts," was disgusted by their filth and laziness, and the party expected no better results when they came to the adjoining Moki reservation.
10124-8{_}1172{_}Here, however, they were happily disappointed, for they arrived at the pueblo of Oraibi, one of the prettiest villages on the mesa, on the eve of one of their characteristic snake dances, and decided to remain over night and see the performance.
10124-8{_}1173{_}Now I am not sure but the "Snake Dance" was so opportune because Uncle John had a private interview with the native chieftain, at which the head Snake Priest and the head Antelope Priest of the tribe were present.
10124-8{_}1174{_}These Indians spoke excellent English and the chief loved the white man's money, so a ceremony that has been held during the month of August for many centuries--long before the Spanish conquistadors found this interesting tribe--was found to be on tap for that very evening.
10124-8{_}1175{_}The girls were tremendously excited at the prospect and Wampus was ordered to prepare camp for the night--the first they had spent in their automobile and away from a hotel.
10124-8{_}1176{_}Not only was the interior of the roomy limousine converted into sleeping quarters for the three girls, but a tent was spread, one side fastened to the car while the other was staked to the ground.
10124-8{_}1177{_}Three wire folding cots came from some hidden place beneath the false bottom of the car, with bedding enough to supply them, and these were for the use of the men in the tent.
10124-8{_}1178{_}The two "bedrooms" having been thus prepared, Wampus lighted the tiny gasoline stove, over which Patsy and Beth enthusiastically cooked the supper.
10124-8{_}1179{_}Beth wanted to "Newburg" the tinned lobster, and succeeded in creaming it very nicely.
10124-8{_}1180{_}They had potato chips, coffee and toasted Holland rusks, as well, and all thoroughly enjoyed the improvised meal.
10124-8{_}1181{_}Their camp had been pitched just at the outskirts of the Indian village, but the snake dance was to take place in a rocky glen some distance away from the pueblo and so Uncle John instructed Wampus to remain and guard their outfit, as the Moki are notorious thieves.
10124-8{_}1182{_}They left the lean little chauffeur perched upon the driver's seat, smoking one of his "stogie" cigars and with Mumbles sitting gravely beside him.
10124-8{_}1183{_}Myrtle hobbled on her crutches between Beth and Patsy, who carried little tin lanterns made with lamp chimneys that had candles inside them.
10124-8{_}1184{_}They first visited the chief, who announced that the ceremonies were about to begin.
10124-8{_}1185{_}At a word from this imposing leader a big Indian caught up Myrtle and easily carried her on his shoulder, as if she were light as a feather, leading the way to the rocky amphitheatre.
10124-8{_}1186{_}Here were assembled all the inhabitants of the village, forming a wide circle around the performers.
10124-8{_}1187{_}The snakes were in a pit dug in the center of the space, over which a few branches had been placed.
10124-8{_}1188{_}This is called the "kisi."
10124-8{_}1189{_}These unique and horrifying snake dances of the Moki have been described so often that I need not speak of this performance in detail.
10124-8{_}1190{_}Before it was half over the girls wished they were back in their automobile; but the Major whispered that for them to leave would cause great offense to the Indians and might result in trouble.
10124-8{_}1191{_}The dance is supposedly a religious one, in honor of the Rain God, and at first the snakes were not used, but as the dancers became wrought up and excited by their antics one by one they reached within the kisi and drew out a snake, allowing the reptiles to coil around their almost naked bodies and handling them with seeming impunity.
10124-8{_}1192{_}A few were harmless species, as bull snakes and arrow snakes; but mostly the Moki used rattlesnakes, which are native to the mesa and its rocky cliffs.
10124-8{_}1193{_}Some travelers have claimed that the fangs of the rattlers are secretly withdrawn before the creatures are handled, but this has been proved to be untrue.
10124-8{_}1194{_}The most accepted theory is that the snakes are never permitted to coil, and cannot strike unless coiled, while the weird chanting and graceful undulating motions of the dancers in some manner "charms" or intoxicates the serpents, which are not aroused to antagonism.
10124-8{_}1195{_}Occasionally, however, one of the Moki priests is bitten, in which case nothing is done to aid him and he is permitted to die, it being considered a judgment of the Rain God for some sin he has committed.
10124-8{_}1196{_}The barbaric rites seemed more picturesque, as well as more revolting, in that they took place by the flickering light of torches and bonfires in a rock strewn plain usually claimed by nature.
10124-8{_}1197{_}When the dancers were more frenzied they held the squirming serpents in their mouths by the middle and allowed them to coil around their necks, dancing wildly the while.
10124-8{_}1198{_}The whole affair was so nauseating and offensive that as soon as it was possible the visitors withdrew and retired to their "camp."
10124-8{_}1199{_}It was now almost midnight, but the path was lighted by the little lanterns they carried.
10124-8{_}1200{_}As they approached the automobile Uncle John was disturbed not to see Wampus at his post.
10124-8{_}1201{_}A light showed from the front of the car, but the chauffeur seemed to be missing.
10124-8{_}1202{_}Coming nearer, however, they soon were greeted by a joyous barking from Mumbles and discovered Wampus squatting upon the ground, puffing at the small end of the cigar and seeming quite composed and tranquil.
10124-8{_}1203{_}"What are you doing there?"
10124-8{_}1204{_}demanded the Major, raising his lantern the better to light the scene.
10124-8{_}1205{_}"I play jailer," grunted Wampus, without moving.
10124-8{_}1206{_}"Him want to steal; Mumble he make bark noise; for me, I steal too--I steal Injun."
10124-8{_}1207{_}A dusky form, prone upon the ground, began to squirm under Wampus, who was then discovered to be sitting upon a big Indian and holding him prisoner.
10124-8{_}1208{_}The chauffeur, partly an Indian himself, knew well how to manage his captive and quieted the fellow by squeezing his throat with his broad stubby fingers.
10124-8{_}1209{_}"How long have you had him there?"
10124-8{_}1210{_}inquired Uncle John, looking at the discomfited "brave" curiously.
10124-8{_}1211{_}"About an hour," was the reply.
10124-8{_}1212{_}"Let him go, then.
10124-8{_}1213{_}We have no prison handy, and the man has perhaps been punished enough."
10124-8{_}1214{_}"I have wait to ask permission to kill him," said Wampus solemnly.
10124-8{_}1215{_}"He know English talk, an' I have told him he is to die.
10124-8{_}1216{_}I have describe, sir, several torture we make on Injun who steal, which make him think he die several time.
10124-8{_}1217{_}So he is now prepare for the worst."
10124-8{_}1218{_}The Indiam squirmed again, and with a sigh Wampus arose and set him free.
10124-8{_}1219{_}"See," he said; "you are save only by mercy of Great White Chief.
10124-8{_}1220{_}You ver' lucky Injun.
10124-8{_}1221{_}But Great White Chief will leave only one eye here when he go away.
10124-8{_}1222{_}If you try to steal again the eye will see, an' then the torture I have describe will be yours.
10124-8{_}1223{_}I am Wampus.
10124-8{_}1224{_}I have spoke."
10124-8{_}1225{_}The Indian listened intently and then slunk away into the darkness without reply.
10124-8{_}1226{_}The night had no further event and in spite of their unusual experiences all slept excellently and awoke in the morning refreshed and ready for new adventures.
10124-8{_}1227{_}CHAPTER IX  NATURE'S MASTERPIECE   From the reservation to the Grand Canyon of the Colorado was not far, but there was no "crosscut" and so they were obliged to make a wide detour nearly to Williams before striking the road that wound upward to the world's greatest wonder.
10124-8{_}1228{_}Slowly and tediously the big car climbed the miserable trail to the rim of the Grand Canyon.
10124-8{_}1229{_}It was night when they arrived, for they had timed it that way, having been told of the marvelous beauty of the canyon by moonlight.
10124-8{_}1230{_}But unfortunately the sky filled with clouds toward evening, and they came to Bright Angel, their destination, in a drizzling rain and total darkness.
10124-8{_}1231{_}The Major was fearful Wampus might run them into the canyon, but the machine's powerful searchlights showed the way clearly and by sticking to the road they finally drew up before an imposing hotel such as you might wonder to find in so remote a spot.
10124-8{_}1232{_}Eagerly enough they escaped from the automobile where they had been shut in and entered the spacious lobby of the hotel, where a merry throng of tourists had gathered.
10124-8{_}1233{_}"Dinner and bed," said Patsy, decidedly.
10124-8{_}1234{_}"I'm all tired out, and poor Myrtle is worn to a frazzle.
10124-8{_}1235{_}There's no chance of seeing the canyon to-night, and as for the dancing, card playing and promiscuous gaiety, it doesn't appeal much to a weary traveler."
10124-8{_}1236{_}The girls were shown to a big room at the front of the hotel, having two beds in it.
10124-8{_}1237{_}A smaller connecting-room was given to Myrtle, while Patsy and Beth shared the larger apartment.
10124-8{_}1238{_}It seems the hotel, big as it was, was fairly filled with guests, the railway running three trains a day to the wonderful canyon; but Uncle John's nieces did not mind occupying the same room, which was comfortably and even luxuriously furnished.
10124-8{_}1239{_}A noise of footsteps along the corridor disturbed Patsy at an early hour.
10124-8{_}1240{_}She opened her eyes to find the room dimly lighted, as by the first streaks of dawn, and sleepily arose to raise the window shade and see if day was breaking.
10124-8{_}1241{_}Her hand still upraised to guide the shade the girl stood as motionless as if turned to stone.
10124-8{_}1242{_}With a long drawn, gasping breath she cried: "Oh, Beth!"
10124-8{_}1243{_}and then stood staring at what is undoubtedly the most entrancing, the most awe inspiring and at the same time the most magnificent spectacle that mortal eye has ever beheld--sunrise above the Grand Canyon of Arizona.
10124-8{_}1244{_}The master painters of the world have gathered in this spot in a vain attempt to transfer the wondrous coloring of the canyon to canvas.
10124-8{_}1245{_}Authors famed for their eloquent command of language have striven as vainly to tell to others what their own eyes have seen; how their senses have been thrilled and their souls uplifted by the marvel that God's hand has wrought.
10124-8{_}1246{_}It can never be pictured.
10124-8{_}1247{_}It can never be described.
10124-8{_}1248{_}Only those who have stood as Patricia Doyle stood that morning and viewed the sublime masterpiece of Nature can realize what those homely words, "The Grand Canyon" mean.
10124-8{_}1249{_}Grand?
10124-8{_}1250{_}It is well named.
10124-8{_}1251{_}Since no other adjective can better describe it, that much abused one may well be accepted to incompletely serve its purpose.
10124-8{_}1252{_}Beth joined her cousin at the window and was instantly as awed and absorbed as Patsy.
10124-8{_}1253{_}Neither remembered Myrtle just then, but fortunately their friend had left the connecting door of their rooms ajar and hearing them stirring came in to see if anything had happened.
10124-8{_}1254{_}She found the two cousins staring intently from the window and went to the second window herself, thus witnessing the spectacle in all its glory.
10124-8{_}1255{_}Even after the magnificent coloring of sunrise had faded the sight was one to rivet the attention.
10124-8{_}1256{_}The hotel seemed built at the very edge of the canyon, and at their feet the ground appeared to fall away and a great gulf yawned that was tinted on all its diverse sides with hues that rivaled those of the rainbow.
10124-8{_}1257{_}Across the chasm they could clearly see the trees and hills; yet these were fully thirteen miles distant, for here is one of the widest portions of the great abyss.
10124-8{_}1258{_}"I'm going to dress," said Beth, breaking the silence at last.
10124-8{_}1259{_}"It seems a sin to stay cooped up in here when such a glorious panorama is at one's feet."
10124-8{_}1260{_}The others did not reply in words, but they all began to dress together with nervous haste, and then made their way down to the canyon's brink.
10124-8{_}1261{_}Others were before them, standing upon the ample porches in interested groups; but such idleness would not content our girls, who trooped away for a more intimate acquaintance with the wonderful gorge.
10124-8{_}1262{_}"Oh, how small--how terribly small--I am!"
10124-8{_}1263{_}cried Patsy, lost in the immensity of the canyon's extent; but this is a common cry of travelers visiting Bright Angel.
10124-8{_}1264{_}You might place a baker's dozen of the huge Falls of Niagara in the Grand Canyon and scarcely notice they were there.
10124-8{_}1265{_}All the vast cathedrals of Europe set upon its plateau would seem like pebbles when viewed from the brink.
10124-8{_}1266{_}The thing is simply incomprehensible to those who have not seen it.
10124-8{_}1267{_}Presently Uncle John and the Major came out to join them and they all wandered along the edge until they came to a huge rock that jutted out far over the monster gulf.
10124-8{_}1268{_}On the furthermost point of this rock, standing with his feet at the very brink, was a tall, thin man, his back toward them.
10124-8{_}1269{_}It seemed a fearful thing to do--to stand where the slightest slip would send him reeling into the abyss.
10124-8{_}1270{_}"It's like tempting fate," whispered Patsy, a safe distance away.
10124-8{_}1271{_}"I wish he would step back a little."
10124-8{_}1272{_}As if he had overheard her the man half turned and calmly examined the group.
10124-8{_}1273{_}His eyes were an almost colorless blue, his features destitute of any expression.
10124-8{_}1274{_}By his dress he seemed well-to-do, if not prosperous, yet there was a hint of melancholy in his poise and about him a definite atmosphere of loneliness.
10124-8{_}1275{_}After that one deliberate look he turned again and faced the canyon, paying no attention to the interested little party that hovered far enough from the edge to avoid any possible danger.
10124-8{_}1276{_}"Oh, dear!"
10124-8{_}1277{_}whispered Myrtle, clinging to Beth's arm with trembling fingers, "I'm afraid he's going to--to commit suicide!"
10124-8{_}1278{_}"Nonsense!"
10124-8{_}1279{_}answered Beth, turning pale nevertheless.
10124-8{_}1280{_}The figure was motionless as before.
10124-8{_}1281{_}Uncle John and the Major started along the path but as Beth attempted to follow them Myrtle broke away from her and hobbled eagerly on her crutches toward the stranger.
10124-8{_}1282{_}She did not go quite to the end of the jutting rock, but stopped some feet away and called in a low, intense voice:  "Don't!"
10124-8{_}1283{_}The man turned again, with no more expression in his eyes or face than before.
10124-8{_}1284{_}He looked at Myrtle steadily a moment, then turned and slowly left the edge, walking to firm ground and back toward the hotel without another glance at the girl.
10124-8{_}1285{_}"I'm so ashamed," said Myrtle, tears of vexation in her eyes as she rejoined her friends.
10124-8{_}1286{_}"But somehow I felt I must warn him--it was an impulse I just couldn't resist."
10124-8{_}1287{_}"Why, no harm resulted, in any event, my dear," returned Beth.
10124-8{_}1288{_}"I wouldn't think of it again."
10124-8{_}1289{_}They took so long a walk that all were nearly famished when they returned to the hotel for breakfast.
10124-8{_}1290{_}Of course Patsy and Beth wanted to go down Bright Angel Trail into the depths of the canyon, for that is the thing all adventurous spirits love to do.
10124-8{_}1291{_}"I'm too fat for such foolishness," said Uncle John, "so I'll stay up here and amuse Myrtle."
10124-8{_}1292{_}The Major decided to go, to "look after our Patsy;" so the three joined the long line of daring tourists and being mounted on docile, sure-footed burros, followed the guide down the trail.
10124-8{_}1293{_}Myrtle and Uncle John spent the morning on the porch of the hotel.
10124-8{_}1294{_}At breakfast the girl had noticed the tall man they had encountered at the canyon's edge quietly engaged in eating at a small table in a far corner of the great dining room.
10124-8{_}1295{_}During the forenoon he came from the hotel to the porch and for a time stood looking far away over the canyon.
10124-8{_}1296{_}Aroused to sympathy by the loneliness of this silent person, Uncle John left his chair and stood beside him at the railing.
10124-8{_}1297{_}"It's a wonderful sight, sir," he remarked in his brisk, sociable way; "wonderful indeed!"
10124-8{_}1298{_}For a moment there was no reply.
10124-8{_}1299{_}"It seems to call one," said the man at length, as if to himself.
10124-8{_}1300{_}"It calls one."
10124-8{_}1301{_}"It's a wonder to me it doesn't call more people to see it," observed Mr. Merrick, cheerfully.
10124-8{_}1302{_}"Think of this magnificent thing--greater and grander than anything the Old World can show, being here right in the heart of America, almost--and so few rush to see it!
10124-8{_}1303{_}Why, in time to come, sir," he added enthusiastically, "not to have seen the Grand Canyon of Arizona will be an admission of inferiority.
10124-8{_}1304{_}It's--it's the biggest thing in all the world!"
10124-8{_}1305{_}The stranger made no reply.
10124-8{_}1306{_}He had not even glanced at Uncle John.
10124-8{_}1307{_}Now he slowly turned and stared fixedly at Myrtle for a moment, till she cast down her eyes, blushing.
10124-8{_}1308{_}Then he re-entered the hotel; nor was he again seen by them.
10124-8{_}1309{_}The little man was indignant at the snub.
10124-8{_}1310{_}Rejoining Myrtle he said to her:  "That fellow wasn't worth saving--if you really saved him, my dear.
10124-8{_}1311{_}He says the canyon calls one, and for all I care he may go to the bottom by any route he pleases."
10124-8{_}1312{_}Which speech showed that gentle, kindly Mr. Merrick was really annoyed.
10124-8{_}1313{_}But a moment later he was all smiles again and Myrtle found him a delightful companion because he knew so well how to read people's thoughts, and if they were sad had a tactful way of cheering them.
10124-8{_}1314{_}The girls and the Major returned from their trip to the plateau full of rapture at their unique experiences.
10124-8{_}1315{_}"I wouldn't have missed it for a million dollars!"
10124-8{_}1316{_}cried the Major; but he added: "and you couldn't hire me to go again for two million!"
10124-8{_}1317{_}"It was great," said Patsy; "but I'm tuckered out."
10124-8{_}1318{_}"I had nineteen narrow escapes from sudden death," began Beth, but her cousin interrupted her by saying: "So had everyone in the party; and if the canyon had caved in we'd all be dead long ago.
10124-8{_}1319{_}Stop your chattering now and get ready for dinner.
10124-8{_}1320{_}I'm nearly starved."
10124-8{_}1321{_}Next morning they took a farewell view of the beautiful scene and then climbed into their automobile to continue their journey.
10124-8{_}1322{_}Many of the tourists had wondered at their temerity in making such a long trip through a poorly settled country in a motor car and had plied them with questions and warnings.
10124-8{_}1323{_}But they were thoroughly enjoying this outing and nothing very disagreeable had happened to them so far.
10124-8{_}1324{_}I am sure that on this bright, glorious morning you could not have hired any one of the party to abandon the automobile and finish the trip by train.
10124-8{_}1325{_}CHAPTER X  A COYOTE SERENADE   The roads were bad enough.
10124-8{_}1326{_}They were especially bad west of Williams.
10124-8{_}1327{_}Just now an association of automobile tourists has been formed to create a boulevard route through from the Atlantic to the Pacific coast, but at the time of this story no attention had been given the roads of the far West and only the paths of the rancheros from town to town served as guides.
10124-8{_}1328{_}On leaving Williams they turned south so as to avoid the more severe mountain roads, and a fine run through a rather uninteresting country brought them to Prescott on the eve of the second day after leaving the Canyon.
10124-8{_}1329{_}Here they decided to take a day's rest, as it was Sunday and the hotel was comfortable; but Monday morning they renewed their journey and headed southwesterly across the alkali plains--called "mesa"--for Parker, on the boundary line between Arizona and California.
10124-8{_}1330{_}Towns of any sort were very scarce in this section and the country was wild and often barren of vegetation for long stretches.
10124-8{_}1331{_}There were some extensive ranches, however, as this is the section favored for settlement by a class of Englishmen called "remittance men."
10124-8{_}1332{_}These are mostly the "black sheep" or outcasts of titled families, who having got into trouble of some sort at home, are sent to America to isolate themselves on western ranches, where they receive monthly or quarterly remittances of money to support them.
10124-8{_}1333{_}The remittance men are poor farmers, as a rule.
10124-8{_}1334{_}They are idle and lazy except when it comes to riding, hunting and similar sports.
10124-8{_}1335{_}Their greatest industry is cattle raising, yet these foreign born "cowboys" constitute an entirely different class from those of American extraction, found in Texas and on the plains of the Central West.
10124-8{_}1336{_}They are educated and to an extent cultured, being "gentlemen born" but sad backsliders in the practise of the profession.
10124-8{_}1337{_}Because other ranchers hesitate to associate with them they congregate in settlements of their own, and here in Arizona, on the banks of the Bill Williams Branch of the Colorado River, they form almost the total population.
10124-8{_}1338{_}Our friends had hoped to make the little town of Gerton for the night, but the road was so bad that Wampus was obliged to drive slowly and carefully, and so could not make very good time.
10124-8{_}1339{_}Accidents began to happen, too, doubtless clue to the hard usage the machine had received.
10124-8{_}1340{_}First a spring broke, and Wampus was obliged to halt long enough to clamp it together with stout steel braces.
10124-8{_}1341{_}An hour later the front tire was punctured by cactus spines, which were thick upon the road.
10124-8{_}1342{_}Such delays seriously interfered with their day's mileage.
10124-8{_}1343{_}Toward sunset Uncle John figured, from the information he had received at Prescott, that they were yet thirty miles from Gerton, and so he decided to halt and make camp while there was yet sufficient daylight remaining to do so conveniently.
10124-8{_}1344{_}"We might hunt for a ranch house and beg for shelter," said he, "but from the stories I've heard of the remittance men I am sure we will enjoy ourselves better if we rely entirely upon our own resources."
10124-8{_}1345{_}The girls were, of course, delighted at the prospect of such an experience, for the silent, solitary mesa made them feel they were indeed "in the wilds of the Great American Desert."
10124-8{_}1346{_}The afternoon had been hot and the ride dusty, but there was now a cooler feeling in the air since the sun had fallen low in the horizon.
10124-8{_}1347{_}They carried their own drinking water, kept ice-cold in thermos bottles, and Uncle John also had a thermos tub filled with small squares of ice.
10124-8{_}1348{_}This luxury, in connection with their ample supply of provisions, enabled the young women to prepare a supper not to be surpassed in any modern hotel.
10124-8{_}1349{_}The soup came from one can, the curried chicken from another, while artichokes, peas, asparagus and plum pudding shed their tin coverings to complete the meal.
10124-8{_}1350{_}Fruits, cheese and biscuits they had in abundance, so there was no hardship in camping out on a deserted Arizona table-land, as far as food was concerned.
10124-8{_}1351{_}The Interior of the limousine, when made into berths for the three girls, was as safe and cosy as a Pullman sleeping coach.
10124-8{_}1352{_}Only the men's quarters, the "lean-to" tent, was in any way open to invasion.
10124-8{_}1353{_}After the meal was ended and the things washed and put away they all sat on folding camp chairs outside the little tent and enjoyed the intense silence surrounding them.
10124-8{_}1354{_}The twilight gradually deepened into darkness.
10124-8{_}1355{_}Wampus kept one of the searchlights lit to add an element of cheerfulness to the scene, and Myrtle was prevailed upon to sing one or two of her simple songs.
10124-8{_}1356{_}She had a clear, sweet voice, although not a strong one, and they all--especially Uncle John--loved to hear her sing.
10124-8{_}1357{_}Afterward they talked over their trip and the anticipated change from this arid region to the verdure of California, until suddenly a long, bloodcurdling howl broke the stillness and caused them one and all to start from their seats.
10124-8{_}1358{_}That is, all but Wampus.
10124-8{_}1359{_}The chauffeur, sitting apart with his black cigar in his mouth, merely nodded and said: "Coyote."
10124-8{_}1360{_}The Major coughed and resumed his seat.
10124-8{_}1361{_}Uncle John stood looking into the darkness as if trying to discern the creature.
10124-8{_}1362{_}"Are coyotes considered dangerous?"
10124-8{_}1363{_}he asked the Canadian.
10124-8{_}1364{_}"Not to us," replied Wampus.
10124-8{_}1365{_}"Sometime, if one man be out on mesa alone, an' plenty coyote come, he have hard fight for life.
10124-8{_}1366{_}Coyote is wild dog.
10124-8{_}1367{_}He is big coward unless pretty hungry.
10124-8{_}1368{_}If I leave light burn he never come near us."
10124-8{_}1369{_}"Then let it burn--all night," said Mr. Merrick.
10124-8{_}1370{_}"There he goes again--and another with him!
10124-8{_}1371{_}What a horrible wail it is."
10124-8{_}1372{_}"I rather like it," said Patsy, with her accustomed calmness.
10124-8{_}1373{_}"It is certainly an added experience to be surrounded by coyotes.
10124-8{_}1374{_}Probably our trip wouldn't have been complete without it."
10124-8{_}1375{_}"A little of that serenade will suffice me," admitted Beth, as the howls grew nearer and redoubled in volume.
10124-8{_}1376{_}Myrtle's eyes were big and earnest.
10124-8{_}1377{_}She was not afraid, but there was something uncanny in being surrounded by such savage creatures.
10124-8{_}1378{_}Nearer and nearer sounded the howls, until it was easy to see a dozen fierce eyes gleaming in the darkness, not a stone's throw away from the camp.
10124-8{_}1379{_}"I guess you girls had better go to bed," remarked Uncle John, a bit nervously.
10124-8{_}1380{_}"There's no danger, you know--none at all.
10124-8{_}1381{_}Let the brutes howl, if they want to--especially as we can't stop them.
10124-8{_}1382{_}But you are tired, my dears, and I'd like to see you settled for the night."
10124-8{_}1383{_}Somewhat reluctantly they entered the limousine, drew the curtains and prepared for bed.
10124-8{_}1384{_}Certainly they were having a novel experience, and if Uncle John would feel easier to have them listen to the howling coyotes from inside the limousine instead of outside, they could not well object to his request.
10124-8{_}1385{_}Presently Wampus asked the Major for his revolver, and on obtaining the weapon he walked a few paces toward the coyotes and fired a shot into their group.
10124-8{_}1386{_}They instantly scattered and made off, only to return in a few moments to their former position.
10124-8{_}1387{_}"Will they continue this Grand Opera chorus all night?"
10124-8{_}1388{_}asked Uncle John.
10124-8{_}1389{_}"Perhap," said Wampus.
10124-8{_}1390{_}"They hungry, an' smell food.
10124-8{_}1391{_}Coyote can no reason.
10124-8{_}1392{_}If he could, he know ver' well we never feed him."
10124-8{_}1393{_}"The next time we come this way let us fetch along a ton or so of coyote feed," suggested the Major.
10124-8{_}1394{_}"I wonder what the poor brutes would think if they were stuffed full for once in their lives?"
10124-8{_}1395{_}"It have never happen, sir," observed Wampus, shaking his head gravely.
10124-8{_}1396{_}"Coyote all born hungry; he live hungry; he die hungry.
10124-8{_}1397{_}If ever coyote was not hungry he would not be coyote."
10124-8{_}1398{_}"In that case, Major," said Uncle John, "let us go to bed and try to sleep.
10124-8{_}1399{_}Perhaps in slumber we may forget these howling fiends."
10124-8{_}1400{_}"Very well," agreed Major Doyle, rising to enter the little tent.
10124-8{_}1401{_}Wampus unexpectedly interposed.
10124-8{_}1402{_}"Wait," called the little chauffeur.
10124-8{_}1403{_}"Jus' a minute, if you please."
10124-8{_}1404{_}While the Major and Mr. Merrick stood wondering at the request, the Canadian, who was still holding the revolver in one hand, picked a steel rod from the rumble of the automobile and pushing aside the flap of the little tent entered.
10124-8{_}1405{_}The tail-lamp of the car burned inside, dimly lighting the place.
10124-8{_}1406{_}The Major was about to follow Wampus when a revolver shot arrested him.
10124-8{_}1407{_}This sound was followed by a quick thumping against the ground of the steel bar, and then Wampus emerged from the tent holding a dark, squirming object on the end of the rod extended before him.
10124-8{_}1408{_}"What is it?"
10124-8{_}1409{_}asked Mr. Merrick, somewhat startled.
10124-8{_}1410{_}"Rattlesnake," said Wampus, tossing the thing into the sagebrush.
10124-8{_}1411{_}"I see him crawl in tent while you eat supper."
10124-8{_}1412{_}"Why did you not tell us?"
10124-8{_}1413{_}cried the Major excitedly.
10124-8{_}1414{_}"I thought him perhaps crawl out again.
10124-8{_}1415{_}Him sometime do that.
10124-8{_}1416{_}But no.
10124-8{_}1417{_}Mister snake he go sleep in tent which is reserve for his superior.
10124-8{_}1418{_}I say nothing, for I do not wish to alarm the young ladies.
10124-8{_}1419{_}That is why I hold the dog Mumble so tight, for he small eye see snake too, an' fool dog wish to go fight him.
10124-8{_}1420{_}Rattlesnake soon eat Mumble up--eh?
10124-8{_}1421{_}But never mind; there is no worry.
10124-8{_}1422{_}I am Wampus, an' I am here.
10124-8{_}1423{_}You go to bed now, an' sleep an' be safe."
10124-8{_}1424{_}He said this rather ostentatiously, and for that reason neither of the others praised his watchful care or his really brave act.
10124-8{_}1425{_}That Wampus was proving himself a capable and faithful servant even the Major was forced to admit, yet the man's bombast and self-praise robbed him of any word of commendation he justly earned.
10124-8{_}1426{_}"I think," said Uncle John, "I'll bunk on the front seat to-night.
10124-8{_}1427{_}I'm short, you see, and will just about curl up in the space.
10124-8{_}1428{_}I believe snakes do not climb up wheels.
10124-8{_}1429{_}Make my bed on the front seat, Wampus."
10124-8{_}1430{_}The man grinned but readily obeyed.
10124-8{_}1431{_}The Major watched him thoughtfully.
10124-8{_}1432{_}"For my part," he said, "I'll have a bed made on top the roof."
10124-8{_}1433{_}"Pshaw!"
10124-8{_}1434{_}said Uncle John; "you'll scratch the paint."
10124-8{_}1435{_}"That is a matter of indifference to me," returned the Major.
10124-8{_}1436{_}"You'll roll off, in your sleep, and hurt yourself."
10124-8{_}1437{_}"I'll risk that, sir."
10124-8{_}1438{_}"Are you afraid, Major?"
10124-8{_}1439{_}"Afraid!
10124-8{_}1440{_}Me?
10124-8{_}1441{_}Not when I'm awake, John.
10124-8{_}1442{_}But what's to prevent more of those vermin from crawling into the tent during the night?"
10124-8{_}1443{_}"Such thing very unusual."
10124-8{_}1444{_}remarked Wampus, placing the last blanket on Mr. Merrick's improvised bed.
10124-8{_}1445{_}"Perhaps you sleep in tent a week an' never see another rattler."
10124-8{_}1446{_}"Just the same," concluded the Major, "I'll have my bed on top the limousine."
10124-8{_}1447{_}He did, Wampus placing blankets and a pillow for him without a word of protest.
10124-8{_}1448{_}The Major climbed over Uncle John and mounted to the roof of the car, which sloped to either side but was broad and long enough to accommodate more than one sleeper.
10124-8{_}1449{_}Being an old campaigner and a shrewd tactician, Major Doyle made two blankets into rolls, which he placed on either side of him, to "anchor" his body in position.
10124-8{_}1450{_}Then he settled himself to rest beneath the brilliant stars while the coyotes maintained their dismal howling.
10124-8{_}1451{_}But a tired man soon becomes insensible to even such annoyances.
10124-8{_}1452{_}The girls, having entered the limousine from the door opposite the tent, were all unaware of the rattlesnake episode and supposed the shot had been directed against the coyotes.
10124-8{_}1453{_}They heard the Major climbing upon the roof, but did not demand any explanation, being deep in those bedtime confidences so dear to all girls.
10124-8{_}1454{_}Even they came to disregard the persistent howls of the coyotes, and in time fell asleep.
10124-8{_}1455{_}Wampus did not seem afraid of snakes.
10124-8{_}1456{_}The little chauffeur went to bed in the tent and slept soundly upon his cot until daybreak, when the coyotes withdrew and the Canadian got up to make the coffee.
10124-8{_}1457{_}The Major peered over the edge of the roof to watch him.
10124-8{_}1458{_}He had a sleepy look about his eyes, as if he had not rested well.
10124-8{_}1459{_}Uncle John was snoring with gentle regularity and the girls were still asleep.
10124-8{_}1460{_}"Wampus," said the Major, "do you know the proper definition of a fool?"
10124-8{_}1461{_}Wampus reflected, stirring the coffee carefully.
10124-8{_}1462{_}"I am not--what you call him?--a dictionairre; no.
10124-8{_}1463{_}But I am Wampus.
10124-8{_}1464{_}I have live much in very few year.
10124-8{_}1465{_}I would say a fool is man who think he is wise.
10124-8{_}1466{_}For what is wise?
10124-8{_}1467{_}Nothing!"
10124-8{_}1468{_}The Major felt comforted.
10124-8{_}1469{_}"It occurred to me," he said, beginning to climb down from the roof, "that a fool was a man who left a good home for this uncomfortable life on a barren desert.
10124-8{_}1470{_}This country wasn't made for humans; it belongs to the coyotes and the rattlesnakes.
10124-8{_}1471{_}What right have we to intrude upon them, then?"
10124-8{_}1472{_}Wampus did not reply.
10124-8{_}1473{_}It was not his business to criticise his employers.
10124-8{_}1474{_}CHAPTER XI  A REAL ADVENTURE AT LAST   Uncle John woke up when the Major inadvertently placed a heel upon his round stomach on the way to the ground.
10124-8{_}1475{_}The chubby little millionaire had slept excellently and was in a genial humor this morning.
10124-8{_}1476{_}He helped Wampus fry the bacon and scramble the eggs, while the Major called the girls.
10124-8{_}1477{_}It proved a glorious sunrise and the air was full of pure ozone.
10124-8{_}1478{_}They had suffered little from cold during the trip, although it was in the dead of winter and the altitude considerable.
10124-8{_}1479{_}Just now they were getting closer to California every hour, and when they descended from the mesa it would gradually grow warmer.
10124-8{_}1480{_}They were all becoming expert at "breaking camp," and preparing for the road.
10124-8{_}1481{_}Beth and Patsy put away the bedding and "made up" the interior of the limousine for traveling.
10124-8{_}1482{_}The Major and Uncle John folded the tent and packed it away, while Wampus attended to the dishes and tinware and then looked over his car.
10124-8{_}1483{_}In a surprisingly short time they were all aboard and the big machine was gliding over the faint trail.
10124-8{_}1484{_}The mesa was not a flat or level country, for they were still near to the mountain ranges.
10124-8{_}1485{_}The way was up hill and down, in gentle slopes, and soon after starting they breasted the brow of a hill and were confronted by half a dozen mounted men, who seemed as much astonished at the encounter as they were.
10124-8{_}1486{_}It being an event to meet anyone in this desolate place Wampus involuntarily brought the car to a halt, while the riders lined up beside it and stared rather rudely at the party.
10124-8{_}1487{_}They were dressed as cowboys usually are, with flannel shirts, chapelets and sombrero hats; but their faces were not rugged nor healthy, as is the case with most Western cowboys, but bore marks of dissipation and hard living.
10124-8{_}1488{_}"Remittance men," whispered Wampus.
10124-8{_}1489{_}Uncle John nodded.
10124-8{_}1490{_}He had heard of this curious class.
10124-8{_}1491{_}Especially were the men staring at the three pretty, feminine faces that peered from the interior of the limousine.
10124-8{_}1492{_}They had remained silent thus far, but now one of them, a fellow with dark eyes and a sallow complexion, reined his horse nearer the car and removed his hat with a sweeping gesture that was not ungraceful.
10124-8{_}1493{_}"A merry morning to you, fair ladies--or angels--I much misdoubt which we have chanced upon.
10124-8{_}1494{_}Anyhow, welcome to Hades!"
10124-8{_}1495{_}Uncle John frowned.
10124-8{_}1496{_}He did not like the bantering, impudent tone.
10124-8{_}1497{_}Beth flushed and turned aside her head; Myrtle shrank back in her corner out of sight; but Patsy glared fixedly at the speaker with an expression that was far from gracious.
10124-8{_}1498{_}The remittance man did not seem daunted by this decided aversion.
10124-8{_}1499{_}A sneering laugh broke from his companions, and one of them cried:  "Back up, Algy, and give your betters a chance.
10124-8{_}1500{_}You're out of it, old man."
10124-8{_}1501{_}"I have no betters," he retorted.
10124-8{_}1502{_}Then, turning to the girls again and ignoring the presence of the men accompanying them, he continued:  "Beauteous visions, since you have wilfully invaded the territory of Hades Ranch, of which diabolical domain I, Algernon Tobey, am by grace of his Satanic majesty the master, I invite you to become my guests and participate in a grand ball which I shall give this evening in your honor."
10124-8{_}1503{_}His comrades laughed again, and one of them shouted:  "Good for you, Algy.
10124-8{_}1504{_}A dance--that's the thing!"
10124-8{_}1505{_}"Why, we haven't had the chance of a dance for ages," said another approvingly.
10124-8{_}1506{_}"Because we have had no ladies to dance with," explained Algy.
10124-8{_}1507{_}"But here are three come to our rescue--perhaps more, if I could see inside that barricade--and they cannot refuse us the pleasure of their society."
10124-8{_}1508{_}"Sir," said Major Doyle, stiffly, "you are pleased to be impertinent.
10124-8{_}1509{_}Ride on, you rascals, and spare us further sight of you."
10124-8{_}1510{_}The man turned upon him a scowling face.
10124-8{_}1511{_}"Don't interfere," he said warningly.
10124-8{_}1512{_}"This isn't your party, you old duffer!"
10124-8{_}1513{_}"Drive ahead, Wampus," commanded Uncle John.
10124-8{_}1514{_}Wampus had to get out and crank the engines, which he calmly proceeded to do.
10124-8{_}1515{_}The man who had called himself Algernon Tobey perceived his intention and urged his pony to the front of the car.
10124-8{_}1516{_}"Let that thing alone.
10124-8{_}1517{_}Keep your hands off!"
10124-8{_}1518{_}he said.
10124-8{_}1519{_}Wampus paid no attention.
10124-8{_}1520{_}The fellow brought his riding whip down sharply on the chauffeur's shoulders, inflicting a stinging blow.
10124-8{_}1521{_}Instantly little Wampus straightened up, grasped Tobey by the leg and with a swift, skillful motion jerked him from his horse.
10124-8{_}1522{_}The man started to draw his revolver, but in an instant he and Wampus were rolling together upon the ground and the Canadian presently came uppermost and held his antagonist firmly between his knees.
10124-8{_}1523{_}Then with deliberation he raised his clinched fist and thrust it forcibly against Mr. Tobey's eye, repeating the impact upon his nose, his chin and his cheek in a succession of jarring thumps that were delivered with scientific precision.
10124-8{_}1524{_}Algy fairly howled, kicking and struggling to be free.
10124-8{_}1525{_}None of his comrades offered to interfere and it seemed they were grimly enjoying the punishment that was being; inflicted upon their leader.
10124-8{_}1526{_}When Wampus had quite finished his work he arose, adjusted his disarranged collar and tie and proceeded to crank the engines.
10124-8{_}1527{_}Then he climbed into his seat and started the car with a sudden bound.
10124-8{_}1528{_}As he did so a revolver shot rang out and one of the front tires, pierced by the bullet, ripped itself nearly in two as it crumpled up.
10124-8{_}1529{_}A shout of derisive laughter came from the cowboys.
10124-8{_}1530{_}Algy was astride his pony again, and as Wampus brought the damaged car to a stop the remittance men dashed by and along the path, taking the same direction Uncle John's party was following".
10124-8{_}1531{_}Tobey held back a little, calling out:  "Au revoir!
10124-8{_}1532{_}I shall expect you all at my party.
10124-8{_}1533{_}I'm going now to get the fiddler."
10124-8{_}1534{_}He rejoined his comrades then, and they all clattered away until a roll of the mesa hid them from sight.
10124-8{_}1535{_}Uncle John got down from his seat to assist his chauffeur.
10124-8{_}1536{_}"Thank you, Wampus," he said.
10124-8{_}1537{_}"Perhaps you should have killed him while you had the opportunity; but you did very well."
10124-8{_}1538{_}Wampus was wrestling with the tire.
10124-8{_}1539{_}"I have never start a private graveyard," he replied, "for reason I am afraid to hurt anyone.
10124-8{_}1540{_}But I am Wampus.
10124-8{_}1541{_}If Mister Algy he dance to-night, somebody mus' lead him, for he will be blind."
10124-8{_}1542{_}"I never met such a lawless brood in my life," prowled the Major, indignantly.
10124-8{_}1543{_}"If they were in New York they'd be put behind the bars in two minutes."
10124-8{_}1544{_}"But they are in Arizona--in the wilderness," said Uncle John gravely.
10124-8{_}1545{_}"If there are laws here such people do not respect them."
10124-8{_}1546{_}It took a long time to set the new tire and inflate it, for the outer tube was torn so badly that an extra one had to be substituted.
10124-8{_}1547{_}But finally the task was accomplished and once more they renewed their journey.
10124-8{_}1548{_}Now that they were alone with their friends the girls were excitedly gossiping over the encounter.
10124-8{_}1549{_}"Do you really suppose we are on that man's ground--his ranch, as he calls it?"
10124-8{_}1550{_}asked Myrtle, half fearfully.
10124-8{_}1551{_}"Why, I suppose someone owns all this ground, barren as it is," replied Patsy.
10124-8{_}1552{_}"But we are following a regular road--not a very good one, nor much traveled; but a road, nevertheless--and any road is public property and open for the use of travelers."
10124-8{_}1553{_}"Perhaps we shall pass by their ranch house," suggested Beth.
10124-8{_}1554{_}"If we do," Uncle John answered, "I'll have Wampus put on full speed.
10124-8{_}1555{_}Even their wild ponies can't follow us then, and if they try shooting up the tires again they are quite likely to miss as we spin by."
10124-8{_}1556{_}"Isn't there any other road?"
10124-8{_}1557{_}the Major asked.
10124-8{_}1558{_}Wampus shook his head.
10124-8{_}1559{_}"I have never come jus' this same route before," he admitted; "but I make good friend in Prescott, who know all Arizona blindfold.
10124-8{_}1560{_}Him say this is nice, easy road and we cannot get lost for a good reason--the reason there is no other road at all--only this one."
10124-8{_}1561{_}"Did your friend say anything about Hades Ranch?"
10124-8{_}1562{_}continued the questioner.
10124-8{_}1563{_}"He say remittance man make much mischief if he can; but he one foreign coward, drunk most time an' when sober weak like my aunt's tea.
10124-8{_}1564{_}He say don't let remittance man make bluff.
10124-8{_}1565{_}No matter how many come, if you hit one they all run."
10124-8{_}1566{_}"H-m," murmured Uncle John, "I'm not so sure of that, Wampus.
10124-8{_}1567{_}There seems to be a good many of those insolent rascals, and I hope we shall not meet them again.
10124-8{_}1568{_}They may give us trouble yet."
10124-8{_}1569{_}"Never be afraid," advised the chauffeur.
10124-8{_}1570{_}"I am Wampus, an' I am here!"
10124-8{_}1571{_}Admitting that evident truth, our tourists were not greatly reassured.
10124-8{_}1572{_}Wampus could not tell where the road might lead them, for he did not know, save that it led by devious winds to Parker, on the border between Arizona and California; but what lay between them and that destination was a sealed book to them all.
10124-8{_}1573{_}The car was heavy and the road soft; so in spite of their powerful engines the car was not making more than fifteen miles an hour.
10124-8{_}1574{_}A short ride brought them to a ridge, from the top of which they saw a huddle of buildings not far distant, with a near-by paddock containing a number of ponies and cattle.
10124-8{_}1575{_}The buildings were not palatial, being composed mostly of adobe and slab wood; but the central one, probably the dwelling or ranch house, was a low, rambling pile covering considerable ground.
10124-8{_}1576{_}The road led directly toward this group of buildings, which our travelers at once guessed to be "Hades Ranch."
10124-8{_}1577{_}Wampus slowed down and cast a sharp glance around, but the land on either side of the trail was thick with cactus and sagebrush and to leave the beaten path meant a puncture almost instantly.
10124-8{_}1578{_}There was but one thing to be done.
10124-8{_}1579{_}"Pretty good road here," said Wampus.
10124-8{_}1580{_}"Hold tight an' don't get scare.
10124-8{_}1581{_}We make a race of it."
10124-8{_}1582{_}"Go ahead," returned Uncle John, grimly.
10124-8{_}1583{_}"If any of those scoundrels get in your way, run them down."
10124-8{_}1584{_}"I never like to hurt peoples; but if that is your command, sir, I will obey," said Wampus, setting his jaws tightly together.
10124-8{_}1585{_}The car gathered speed and shot over the road at the rate of twenty miles an hour; then twenty-five--then thirty--and finally forty.
10124-8{_}1586{_}The girls sat straight and looked eagerly ahead.
10124-8{_}1587{_}Forms were darting here and there among the buildings of the ranch, quickly congregating in groups on either side of the roadway.
10124-8{_}1588{_}A red flag fluttered in the center of the road, some four feet from the ground.
10124-8{_}1589{_}"Look out!"
10124-8{_}1590{_}shouted Uncle John.
10124-8{_}1591{_}"Stop, Wampus; stop her, I say!"
10124-8{_}1592{_}Wampus saw why, and applied his brakes.
10124-8{_}1593{_}The big car trembled, slowed down, and came to a stop less than a foot away from three ugly bars of barbed wire which had been placed across the road.
10124-8{_}1594{_}They were now just beside the buildings, and a triumphant shout greeted them from their captors, the remittance men.
10124-8{_}1595{_}CHAPTER XII  CAPTURED   "Welcome to Hades!"
10124-8{_}1596{_}cried a stout little man in a red blouse, sticking his leering countenance through the door of the limousine.
10124-8{_}1597{_}"Shut up, Stubby," commanded a hoarse voice from the group.
10124-8{_}1598{_}"Haven't you any manners?
10124-8{_}1599{_}You haven't been introduced yet."
10124-8{_}1600{_}"I've engaged the dark eyed one for the first dance," persisted Stubby, as a dozen hands dragged him away from the door.
10124-8{_}1601{_}The Major sprang out and confronted the band.
10124-8{_}1602{_}"What are we to understand by this outrage?"
10124-8{_}1603{_}he demanded fiercely.
10124-8{_}1604{_}"It means you are all invited to a party, and we won't accept any regrets," replied a laughing voice.
10124-8{_}1605{_}Patsy put her head out of the window and looked at the speaker.
10124-8{_}1606{_}It was Mr. Algernon Tobey.
10124-8{_}1607{_}He had two strips of sticking plaster over his nose.
10124-8{_}1608{_}One of his eyes was swollen shut and the other was almost closed.
10124-8{_}1609{_}Yet he spoke in a voice more cheerful than it was when they first met him.
10124-8{_}1610{_}"Don't be afraid," he added.
10124-8{_}1611{_}"No one has the slightest intention of injuring any of you in any way, I assure you."
10124-8{_}1612{_}"We have not the same intention in regard to you, sir," replied Major Doyle, fuming with rage, for his "Irish was up," as he afterward admitted.
10124-8{_}1613{_}"Unless you at once remove that barricade and allow us to proceed we will not be responsible for what happens.
10124-8{_}1614{_}You are warned, sir!"
10124-8{_}1615{_}Uncle John, by this time standing beside the Major upon the ground, had been quietly "sizing up the situation," as he would have expressed it.
10124-8{_}1616{_}He found they had been captured by a party of fourteen men, most of whom were young, although three or four, including Tobey, were of middle age.
10124-8{_}1617{_}The atmosphere of the place, with its disorderly surroundings and ill kept buildings, indicated that Hades Ranch was bachelor quarters exclusively.
10124-8{_}1618{_}Half a dozen Mexicans and one or two Chinamen were in the background, curious onlookers.
10124-8{_}1619{_}Mr. Merrick noted the fact that the remittance men were an unkempt, dissipated looking crew, but that their faces betokened reckless good humor rather than desperate evil.
10124-8{_}1620{_}There was no doubt but most of them were considering this episode in the light of a joke, and were determined to enjoy the experience at the expense of their enforced guests.
10124-8{_}1621{_}Uncle John had lived many years in the West and knew something of these peculiar English exiles.
10124-8{_}1622{_}Therefore he was neither frightened nor unduly angry, but rather annoyed by the provoking audacity of the fellows.
10124-8{_}1623{_}He had three young girls to protect and knew these men could not be fit acquaintances for them.
10124-8{_}1624{_}But he adopted a tone different from the Major's and addressed himself to Tobey as the apparent leader of the band.
10124-8{_}1625{_}"Sir," he said calmly but with pointed emphasis, "I believe you were born a gentleman, as were your comrades here."
10124-8{_}1626{_}"You are right," answered Tobey.
10124-8{_}1627{_}"And each and every one you see before you has fallen from his former high estate--through no fault of his own."
10124-8{_}1628{_}This may have been a sarcasm, for the others laughed in boisterous approval.
10124-8{_}1629{_}"In some respects we are still gentlemen," Tobey went on, "but in others we are not to be trusted.
10124-8{_}1630{_}Be reasonable, sir--I haven't the faintest idea who you are or what your name is--and consider calmly our proposition.
10124-8{_}1631{_}Here we are, a number of young fellows who have seen better and happier days, living alone in the midst of an alkali desert.
10124-8{_}1632{_}Most of us haven't seen a female for months, nor a lady for years.
10124-8{_}1633{_}Why, last fall Stubby there rode eighty miles to Buxton, just to stand on a corner and see a lot of greasy Mexican women go by.
10124-8{_}1634{_}We tire of exclusive male society, you see.
10124-8{_}1635{_}We get to bore one another terribly.
10124-8{_}1636{_}So here, like a visitation from heaven, three attractive young ladies descend upon us, traveling through our domain, and having discovered their presence we instantly decided to take advantage of the opportunity and invite them to an impromptu ball.
10124-8{_}1637{_}There's no use refusing us, for we insist on carrying out our plan.
10124-8{_}1638{_}If you men, perhaps the fathers of the young ladies, behave reasonably, we will entertain you royally and send you on your way rejoicing.
10124-8{_}1639{_}Won't we, boys?"
10124-8{_}1640{_}They shouted approval.
10124-8{_}1641{_}"But if you oppose us and act ugly about this fête, gentlemen, we shall be obliged to put a few bullets into you, and decide afterward what disposition to make of the girls.
10124-8{_}1642{_}About the best stunt we do is shooting.
10124-8{_}1643{_}We can't work; we're too poor to gamble much; but we hunt a good bit and we can shoot straight.
10124-8{_}1644{_}I assure you we wouldn't mind losing and taking a few lives if a scrimmage is necessary.
10124-8{_}1645{_}Eh, boys?"
10124-8{_}1646{_}"That's right, Algy," said one, answering for the others; "we'll have that dance if we die for it--ev'ry man Jack of us."
10124-8{_}1647{_}Myrtle was trembling in her corner of the limousine.
10124-8{_}1648{_}Beth sat still with a curl on her lips.
10124-8{_}1649{_}But Patsy was much interested in the proceedings and had listened attentively to the above conversation.
10124-8{_}1650{_}Now the girl suddenly swung open the door and sprang out beside her father, facing the group of cowboys.
