10124-8{_}1651{_}"I am Patricia Doyle," she said in a clear voice, "and these gentlemen," indicating the Major and Mr. Merrick, "are my father and my uncle.
10124-8{_}1652{_}You understand perfectly why they object to the arrangement you suggest, as any one of you would object, had you a daughter in a like position.
10124-8{_}1653{_}But you are arbitrary and not inclined to respect womanhood.
10124-8{_}1654{_}Therefore but one course is open to us--to submit under protest to the unwelcome attentions you desire to thrust upon us."
10124-8{_}1655{_}They listened silently to this frank speech, and some of their faces wore crestfallen expressions by the time she had finished.
10124-8{_}1656{_}Indeed, one of the older men turned on his heel and walked away, disappearing among the buildings.
10124-8{_}1657{_}After a brief hesitation a delicate young fellow--almost a boy--followed this man, his face flaming red with shame.
10124-8{_}1658{_}But the others stood their ground.
10124-8{_}1659{_}"Very good, Miss Doyle," remarked Tobey, with forced cheerfulness.
10124-8{_}1660{_}"You are quite sensible to submit to the inevitable.
10124-8{_}1661{_}Bring out your friends and introduce them, and then we'll all go in to luncheon and prepare for the dance."
10124-8{_}1662{_}"I won't submit to this!"
10124-8{_}1663{_}cried the Major, stamping his foot angrily.
10124-8{_}1664{_}"Yes, you will," said Uncle John, with a motion preventing his irate brother-in-law from drawing a revolver, "Patsy is quite right, and we will submit with as much dignity as we can muster, being overpowered by numbers."
10124-8{_}1665{_}He beckoned to Beth, who stepped out of the car and assisted Myrtle to follow her.
10124-8{_}1666{_}A little cheer of bravado had arisen from the group, inspired by their apparent victory; but when Myrtle's crutches appeared and they saw the fair, innocent face of the young girl who rested upon them, the shout died away in a hush of surprise.
10124-8{_}1667{_}"This is my cousin, Elizabeth De Graf," announced Patsy, with cold deliberation, determined that the proprieties should be observed in all intercourse with these people.
10124-8{_}1668{_}"And I present our friend, Myrtle Dean.
10124-8{_}1669{_}Under ordinary circumstances I believe Myrtle would be excused from dancing, but I suppose no brute in the form of a man would have consideration for her infirmity."
10124-8{_}1670{_}This time even Tobey flushed.
10124-8{_}1671{_}"You've a sharp tongue, Miss Doyle, and it's liable to lead you into trouble," he retorted, losing for the moment his suave demeanor.
10124-8{_}1672{_}"We may be brutes--and I imagine we are--but we're not dangerous unless provoked."
10124-8{_}1673{_}It was savagely said, and Uncle John took warning and motioned Patsy to be silent.
10124-8{_}1674{_}"Lead the way, sir," he said.
10124-8{_}1675{_}"Our chauffeur will of course remain with the car."
10124-8{_}1676{_}Wampus had kept his seat, motionless and silent.
10124-8{_}1677{_}He only nodded in answer to Mr. Merrick's instructions and was entirely disregarded by the remittance men.
10124-8{_}1678{_}The man called "Stubby," who had a round, good-humored face, stepped eagerly to Myrtle's side and exclaimed: "Let me assist you, please."
10124-8{_}1679{_}"No," she said, shaking her head with a wan smile; "I am quite able to walk alone."
10124-8{_}1680{_}He followed her, though, full of interest and with an air of deep respect that belied his former actions.
10124-8{_}1681{_}Tobey, content with his present success, walked beside Mr. Merrick and led the procession toward the ranch house.
10124-8{_}1682{_}The Major followed, his tall form upright, his manner bellicose and resentful, with Beth and Patsy on either side of him.
10124-8{_}1683{_}The remittance men followed in a straggling crowd, laughing and boisterously talking among themselves.
10124-8{_}1684{_}Just as they reached the house a horseman came clattering down the road and all paused involuntarily to mark the new arrival.
10124-8{_}1685{_}The rider was a handsome, slim young fellow, dressed as were the other cowboys present, and he came on at a breakneck speed that seemed only warranted by an errand of life and death.
10124-8{_}1686{_}In front of him, tied to the saddle, appeared a huge bundle, and as the horse dashed up to the group standing by the ranch house the rider gracefully threw himself off and removed his hat with a sweeping gesture as he observed the young ladies.
10124-8{_}1687{_}"I've got him, Algy!"
10124-8{_}1688{_}he cried merrily.
10124-8{_}1689{_}"Dan'l?"
10124-8{_}1690{_}asked Tobey.
10124-8{_}1691{_}"Dan'l himself."
10124-8{_}1692{_}He pointed to the bundle, which heaved and wriggled to show it was alive.
10124-8{_}1693{_}"He refused to come willingly, of course; so I brought him anyhow.
10124-8{_}1694{_}Never yet was there a fiddler willing to be accommodating."
10124-8{_}1695{_}"Good for you, Tim!"
10124-8{_}1696{_}shouted a dozen voices.
10124-8{_}1697{_}And Stubby added in his earnest way; "Dan'l was never more needed in his life."
10124-8{_}1698{_}Tobey was busy unwinding a long lariat that bent the captive nearly double and secured him firmly to the panting horse.
10124-8{_}1699{_}When the bonds were removed Dan'l would have tumbled prone to the ground had not willing hands caught him and supported him upon his feet.
10124-8{_}1700{_}Our friends then observed that he was an aged man with a face thickly furrowed with wrinkles.
10124-8{_}1701{_}He had but one eye, small and gray and very shrewd in expression, which he turned contemptuously upon the crowd surrounding him.
10124-8{_}1702{_}Numb and trembling from his cramped position upon the horse and the terrible jouncing he had endured, the fiddler could scarcely stand at first and shook as with a palsy; but he made a brave effort to control his weakness and turned smilingly at the murmur of pity and indignation that came from the lips of the girls.
10124-8{_}1703{_}"Where's the fiddle?"
10124-8{_}1704{_}demanded Tobey, and Tim unhooked a calico bag from the saddlebow and held it out.
10124-8{_}1705{_}A laugh greeted the gesture.
10124-8{_}1706{_}"Dan'l said he be hanged if he'd come," announced Tim, with a grim appreciation of the humorous side of the situation; "so I hung him and brought him along--and his fiddle to boot.
10124-8{_}1707{_}But don't boot it until after the dance."
10124-8{_}1708{_}"What do you mean, sir, by this rebellious attitude?"
10124-8{_}1709{_}questioned Tobey, sticking his damaged face close to that of the fiddler.
10124-8{_}1710{_}Dan'l blinked with his one eye but refused to answer.
10124-8{_}1711{_}"I've a good mind to skin you alive," continued the leader, in a savage tone.
10124-8{_}1712{_}"You'll either obey my orders or I'll throw you into the snake pit."
10124-8{_}1713{_}"Let him alone, Algy," said Tim, carelessly.
10124-8{_}1714{_}"The old scoundrel has been tortured enough already.
10124-8{_}1715{_}But I see we have partners for the dance," looking critically at the girls, "and I claim first choice because I've brought the fiddler."
10124-8{_}1716{_}At this a roar of protest arose and Tobey turned and said sullenly:  "Come in, all of you.
10124-8{_}1717{_}We'll settle the order of dancing later on."
10124-8{_}1718{_}The interior of the ranch house was certainly picturesque.
10124-8{_}1719{_}A great living room ran all across the front, with an immense fireplace built of irregular adobe bricks.
10124-8{_}1720{_}The floor was strewn with skins of animals--mostly coyotes, a few deer and one or two mountain lions--and the walls were thickly hung with weapons and trophies of the chase.
10124-8{_}1721{_}A big table in one corner was loaded with bottles and glasses, indicating the intemperate habits of the inmates, while on the chimney shelf were rows of pipes and jars of tobacco.
10124-8{_}1722{_}An odor similar to that of a barroom hung over the place which the air from the open windows seemed unable to dissipate.
10124-8{_}1723{_}There were plenty of benches and chairs, with a long mess table occupying the center of the room.
10124-8{_}1724{_}In a corner was an old square piano, which a Mexican was trying to dust as the party entered.
10124-8{_}1725{_}"Welcome to Hades!"
10124-8{_}1726{_}exclaimed Tobey, with an absurd gesture.
10124-8{_}1727{_}"Be good enough to make yourselves at home and I'll see if those devils of Chinamen are getting luncheon ready."
10124-8{_}1728{_}Silently the prisoners sat down.
10124-8{_}1729{_}The crowd poured in after them and disposed themselves in various attitudes about the big room, all staring with more or less boldness at the three girls.
10124-8{_}1730{_}Dan'l the fiddler was pushed in with the others and given a seat, while two or three of the imitation cowboys kept guard over him to prevent any possible escape.
10124-8{_}1731{_}So far the old man had not addressed a word to anyone.
10124-8{_}1732{_}With the absence of the leader the feeling of restraint seemed to relax.
10124-8{_}1733{_}The cowboys began whispering among themselves and chuckling with glee, as if they were enjoying some huge joke.
10124-8{_}1734{_}Stubby had placed himself near the three young ladies, whom he eyed with adoring glances, and somehow none of the prisoners regarded this childish young fellow in exactly the same light as they did his comrades.
10124-8{_}1735{_}Tim, his attitude full of grace as he lounged against a settle, was also near the group.
10124-8{_}1736{_}He seemed a bit thoughtful since his dramatic arrival and had little to say to anyone.
10124-8{_}1737{_}Mr. Merrick engaged Stubby in conversation.
10124-8{_}1738{_}"Does Mr. Tobey own this place?"
10124-8{_}1739{_}he asked.
10124-8{_}1740{_}"By proxy, yes," was the reply.
10124-8{_}1741{_}"It isn't in his name, you know, although that doesn't matter, for he couldn't sell his desert ranch if he had a title to it.
10124-8{_}1742{_}I suppose that is what his folks were afraid of.
10124-8{_}1743{_}Algy is the fourth son of old Lord Featherbone, and got into a disgraceful mess in London some years ago.
10124-8{_}1744{_}So Featherbone shipped him over here, in charge of a family solicitor who hunted out this sequestered spot, bought a couple of thousand acres and built this hut.
10124-8{_}1745{_}Then he went home and left Algy here to keep up the place on a paltry ten pounds--fifty dollars--a month."
10124-8{_}1746{_}"Can he manage to do that?"
10124-8{_}1747{_}asked Uncle John.
10124-8{_}1748{_}"Why, he has to, you see.
10124-8{_}1749{_}He's got together a few cattle, mostly stolen I imagine; but he doesn't try to work the land.
10124-8{_}1750{_}Moreover he's established this community, composed of his suffering fellow exiles, the secret of which lies in the fact that we work the cooperative plan, and all chip in our remittances to boil the common pot.
10124-8{_}1751{_}We can keep more servants and buy more food and drink, that way, than if each one of us lived separately."
10124-8{_}1752{_}"Up in Oregon," said Mr. Merrick, "I've known of some very successful and prosperous ranchmen among the remittance men."
10124-8{_}1753{_}"Oh, we're all kinds, I suppose, good and bad," admitted Stubby.
10124-8{_}1754{_}"This crew's mostly bad, and they're moderately proud of it.
10124-8{_}1755{_}It's a devil of a life, sir, and Hades Ranch is well named.
10124-8{_}1756{_}I've only been here a month.
10124-8{_}1757{_}Had a little property up North; but the sheriff took it for debt, and that forced me to Algy, whom I detest.
10124-8{_}1758{_}I think I'll move on, before long.
10124-8{_}1759{_}But you see I'm limited.
10124-8{_}1760{_}Can't leave Arizona or I'll get my remittance cut off."
10124-8{_}1761{_}"Why were you sent here into exile?"
10124-8{_}1762{_}asked Myrtle artlessly.
10124-8{_}1763{_}He turned red and refused to meet her eyes.
10124-8{_}1764{_}"Went wrong, Miss," he said, "and my folks wouldn't stand for it.
10124-8{_}1765{_}We're all in the same boat," sweeping his arm around, "doing punishment for our misdeeds."
10124-8{_}1766{_}"Do none of you ever reform?"
10124-8{_}1767{_}inquired Patsy.
10124-8{_}1768{_}"What's the use?
10124-8{_}1769{_}We're so far away from home no one there would ever believe in our reformation.
10124-8{_}1770{_}Once we become outcasts, that's the end of our careers.
10124-8{_}1771{_}We're buried in these Western wilds and allowed just enough to keep alive."
10124-8{_}1772{_}"I would think," said Uncle John musingly, "that the manly way would be to cut yourself off entirely from your people at home and go to some city in the United States where honesty and industry would win a new name for you.
10124-8{_}1773{_}Then you could be respected and happy and become of use to the world."
10124-8{_}1774{_}Stubby laughed.
10124-8{_}1775{_}"That has been tried," he replied; "but few ever made a success of it.
10124-8{_}1776{_}We're generally the kind that prefers idleness to work.
10124-8{_}1777{_}My family is wealthy, and I don't mind taking from them what little they give me willingly and all that I can screw out of them besides.
10124-8{_}1778{_}I'm in for life, as the saying is, and I've no especial ambition except to drink myself to death as soon as possible."
10124-8{_}1779{_}Patsy shuddered.
10124-8{_}1780{_}It seemed a horrible thing to be so utterly hopeless.
10124-8{_}1781{_}Could this young fellow have really merited his fate?
10124-8{_}1782{_}CHAPTER XIII  THE FIDDLER   Tim had listened carelessly to the conversation until now, when he said listlessly:  "Don't think us all criminals, for we're not.
10124-8{_}1783{_}In my own case I did nothing to deserve exile except that I annoyed my elder brother by becoming more popular with our social set than he was.
10124-8{_}1784{_}He had all the property and I was penniless, so he got rid of me by threatening to cut off my allowance unless I went to America and stayed there."
10124-8{_}1785{_}"And you accepted such a condition?"
10124-8{_}1786{_}cried Patsy, scornfully.
10124-8{_}1787{_}"Why were you not independent enough to earn your own living?"
10124-8{_}1788{_}He shrugged his shoulders, yet seemed amused.
10124-8{_}1789{_}"I simply couldn't," said he.
10124-8{_}1790{_}"I was not educated to work, you know, and to do so at home would be to disgrace my noble family.
10124-8{_}1791{_}I've too much respect for my lineage to labor with my hands or head."
10124-8{_}1792{_}"But here in America no one would know you," suggested Beth.
10124-8{_}1793{_}"I would only humiliate myself by undertaking such a task.
10124-8{_}1794{_}And why should I do so?
10124-8{_}1795{_}While I am in America my affectionate brother, the head of the family, supports me, as is his duty.
10124-8{_}1796{_}Your philosophy is pretty enough, but it is not practical.
10124-8{_}1797{_}The whole fault lies in our old-fashioned system of inheritance, the elder male of a family getting all the estate and the younger ones nothing at all.
10124-8{_}1798{_}Here, in this crude and plebeian country, I believe it is the custom to provide for all one's children, and a father is at liberty to do so because his estate is not entailed."
10124-8{_}1799{_}"And he earns it himself and can do what he likes with it," added Uncle John, impatiently.
10124-8{_}1800{_}"Your system of inheritance and entail may be somewhat to blame, but your worst fault is in rearing a class of mollycoddles and social drones who are never of benefit to themselves or the world at large.
10124-8{_}1801{_}You, sir, I consider something less than a man."
10124-8{_}1802{_}"I agree with you," replied Tim, readily.
10124-8{_}1803{_}"I'm only good to cumber the earth, and if I get little pleasure out of life I must admit that it's all I'm entitled to."
10124-8{_}1804{_}"And you can't break your bonds and escape?"
10124-8{_}1805{_}asked Patsy.
10124-8{_}1806{_}"I don't care to.
10124-8{_}1807{_}People who are ambitious to do things merely bore me.
10124-8{_}1808{_}I don't admire them or care to imitate them."
10124-8{_}1809{_}From that moment they took no further interest in the handsome outcast.
10124-8{_}1810{_}His world was not their world.
10124-8{_}1811{_}And now Tobey came in, driving before him a lot of Mexicans bearing trays of food.
10124-8{_}1812{_}The long table was laid in a moment, for everything was dumped upon it without any attempt at order.
10124-8{_}1813{_}Each of the cowboys seized a plate from a pile at one end and helped himself to whatever he wanted.
10124-8{_}1814{_}Two or three of the men, however, were courteous enough to attend to their unwilling guests and see they were served as well as conditions would permit The food was plentiful and of good quality, but although none of Uncle John's party was squeamish or a stickler for form, all more or less revolted from the utter disregard of all the proprieties.
10124-8{_}1815{_}"I'm sorry we have no wine; but there's plenty of whiskey, if you like it," remarked Tobey.
10124-8{_}1816{_}The girls were silent and ate little, although they could not help being interested in observing the bohemianism of these gently reared but decadent sons of respectable English families.
10124-8{_}1817{_}As soon as they could they left the table, and Tobey, observing their uneasiness in spite of his damaged and nearly useless optics, decided to send them to another room where they could pass the afternoon without further annoyance.
10124-8{_}1818{_}Stubby escorted the party and ushered them into a good sized room which he said was "Algy's study," although no one ever studied there.
10124-8{_}1819{_}"Algy's afraid you'll balk at the dance; so he wants to please you however he can," remarked the round faced youth.
10124-8{_}1820{_}"You won't mind being left alone, will you?"
10124-8{_}1821{_}"We prefer it, sir," answered the Major, stiffly.
10124-8{_}1822{_}"You see, we're going to have a rare lark this afternoon," continued Stubby, confidentially.
10124-8{_}1823{_}"Usually it's pretty dull here, and all we can do is ride and hunt--play cards and quarrel.
10124-8{_}1824{_}But your coming has created no end of excitement and this dance will be our red-letter day for a long time to come.
10124-8{_}1825{_}The deuce of if is, however, that there are only two girls to dance with thirteen men.
10124-8{_}1826{_}We limit our community to fifteen, you know; but little Ford and old Rutledge have backed down and won't have anything to do with this enterprise.
10124-8{_}1827{_}I don't know why," he continued, thoughtfully.
10124-8{_}1828{_}"Perhaps they still have some gentlemanly instincts," suggested Patsy.
10124-8{_}1829{_}"That must be it," he replied in a relieved tone.
10124-8{_}1830{_}"Well, anyhow, to avoid quarrels and bloodshed we've agreed to throw dice for the dances.
10124-8{_}1831{_}Every one is to have an equal chance, you see, and when you young ladies open the dance the entire programme will be arranged for you."
10124-8{_}1832{_}"Are we to have no choice in the matter of partners?"
10124-8{_}1833{_}inquired Beth curiously.
10124-8{_}1834{_}"None whatever.
10124-8{_}1835{_}There would surely be a row, in that case, and we intend to have everything; pass off pleasantly if we have to kill a few to keep the peace."
10124-8{_}1836{_}With this Stubby bowed low and retreated toward the door, which suddenly opened to admit old Dan'l the fiddler, who was thrust in so violently that his body collided with that of Stubby and nearly knocked him over.
10124-8{_}1837{_}"That's all right," laughed the remittance man, recovering from the shock.
10124-8{_}1838{_}"You mustn't escape, you know, Dan'l, for we depend on you for the music."
10124-8{_}1839{_}He closed the door as he went out and they all heard a bolt shoot into place.
10124-8{_}1840{_}Yet the broad window, scarcely six feet from the ground, stood wide open to admit the air.
10124-8{_}1841{_}Dan'l stood in the middle of the room, motionless for a moment.
10124-8{_}1842{_}Then he raised his wrinkled face and clinched his fists, shaking them in the direction of the living-room.
10124-8{_}1843{_}"Me!"
10124-8{_}1844{_}he muttered; "me play for dese monkeys to dance--me!
10124-8{_}1845{_}a maestro--a composer--a artiste!
10124-8{_}1846{_}No; I vill nod!
10124-8{_}1847{_}I vill die before I condescention to such badness, such mockery!"
10124-8{_}1848{_}They were the first words he had spoken since his arrival, and they seemed to hold all his pentup indignation.
10124-8{_}1849{_}The girls pitied the old man and, recognizing in him a fellow prisoner, sought to comfort him.
10124-8{_}1850{_}"If the dance depends upon us, there will be no dance," said Patsy, firmly.
10124-8{_}1851{_}"I thought you advised submitting to the whim of these ruffians," said Uncle John in surprise.
10124-8{_}1852{_}"Only to gain time, Uncle.
10124-8{_}1853{_}And the scheme has succeeded.
10124-8{_}1854{_}Now is our time to plot and plan how to outwit our enemies."
10124-8{_}1855{_}"Goot!"
10124-8{_}1856{_}cried Dan'l approvingly.
10124-8{_}1857{_}"I help you.
10124-8{_}1858{_}Dey are vermin--pah!
10124-8{_}1859{_}I vould kill dem all mitout mercifulness, unt be glad!"
10124-8{_}1860{_}"It won't be necessary to kill them, I hope," said Beth, smiling.
10124-8{_}1861{_}"All we wish is to secure our escape."
10124-8{_}1862{_}"Vot a time dey make me!"
10124-8{_}1863{_}said Dan'l, more calmly.
10124-8{_}1864{_}"You see, I am living peacefulness in mine bungalow by der river--ten mile away.
10124-8{_}1865{_}Dot brute Tim, he come unt ask me to fiddle for a dance.
10124-8{_}1866{_}I--fiddle!
10124-8{_}1867{_}Ven I refuse me to do it, he tie me up unt by forcibleness elope mit me.
10124-8{_}1868{_}Iss id nod a crime--a vickedness--eh?"
10124-8{_}1869{_}"It certainly is, sir," said Uncle John.
10124-8{_}1870{_}"But do not worry.
10124-8{_}1871{_}These girls have some plan in their heads, I'm sure, and if we manage to escape we will carry you home in safety.
10124-8{_}1872{_}Now, my dears, what is it?"
10124-8{_}1873{_}"Oh, we've only begun to think yet," said Patsy, and walked to the window.
10124-8{_}1874{_}All but Myrtle and Dan'l followed her.
10124-8{_}1875{_}Below the window was a jungle of cactus, with hundreds of spines as slender and sharp as stilettos sticking in every direction.
10124-8{_}1876{_}"H-m; this room is burglar proof," muttered Uncle John, with marked disappointment.
10124-8{_}1877{_}"It also makes an excellent prison," added Patsy.
10124-8{_}1878{_}"But I suspected something of this sort when I saw they had left the window open.
10124-8{_}1879{_}We can't figure on getting out that way, you see."
10124-8{_}1880{_}"Id vould be suiciding," Dan'l said, mournfully shaking his head.
10124-8{_}1881{_}"If dese fiends were as goot as dey are clefer, dey vould be angels."
10124-8{_}1882{_}"No argument seems to prevail with them," remarked Beth.
10124-8{_}1883{_}"They are lawless and merciless, and in this far-away country believe they may do as they please."
10124-8{_}1884{_}"They're as bad as the bandits of Taormina," observed Patsy, smiling at the recollection of an adventure they had abroad; "but we must find some way to evade them."
10124-8{_}1885{_}Dan'l had gone over to Myrtle's corner and stood staring at her with his one shrewd eye.
10124-8{_}1886{_}Uncle John looked thoughtfully out of the window and saw Wampus busy in the road before the house.
10124-8{_}1887{_}He had his coat off and was cutting the bars of barbed wire and rolling them out of the way, while Mumbles, who had been left with him, ran here and there at his heels as if desiring to assist him.
10124-8{_}1888{_}From the big hall, or living room, at the right came a dull roar of voices, subdued shouts and laughter, mingled with the clinking of glasses.
10124-8{_}1889{_}All the remittance men were gathered there deep in the game of dice which was to determine the order in which they were to dance with Beth and Patsy.
10124-8{_}1890{_}The servants were out of sight.
10124-8{_}1891{_}Wampus had the field to himself.
10124-8{_}1892{_}"Come here," said Uncle John to the girls, and when they stood beside him pointed to the car.
10124-8{_}1893{_}"Wampus is making ready for the escape," he continued.
10124-8{_}1894{_}"He has cleared the road and the way is now open if we can manage to get to the machine.
10124-8{_}1895{_}Has your plan matured yet?"
10124-8{_}1896{_}Patsy shook her head.
10124-8{_}1897{_}"Not yet, Uncle," she replied.
10124-8{_}1898{_}"Couldn't Wampus throw us a rope?"
10124-8{_}1899{_}inquired the Major.
10124-8{_}1900{_}"He could," said Uncle John; "but we would be unable to use it.
10124-8{_}1901{_}Those terrible cactus spines are near enough to spear anyone who dared try to slide down a rope.
10124-8{_}1902{_}Think of something else."
10124-8{_}1903{_}They all tried to do that, but no practical idea seemed forthcoming.
10124-8{_}1904{_}"Oh, no," Dan'l was saying to Myrtle; "dey are nod afraid to shoot; bud dey vill nod shoot ladies, belief me.
10124-8{_}1905{_}Always dey carry refolfers in deir belts--or deir holsterses.
10124-8{_}1906{_}Dey eat mit refolfers; dey schleep mit refolfers; dey hunt, dey quarrel, unt sometimes dey shoot each odder--de best enactionment vot dey do.
10124-8{_}1907{_}Bud dey do nod shoot at ladies--nefer."
10124-8{_}1908{_}"Will they wear their revolvers at the dance?"
10124-8{_}1909{_}asked Beth, overhearing this speech.
10124-8{_}1910{_}"I belief id," said Dan'l, wagging his ancient head.
10124-8{_}1911{_}"Dey like to be ready to draw quick like, if anybody shteps on anybody's toes.
10124-8{_}1912{_}Yes; of course."
10124-8{_}1913{_}"What a horrible idea!"
10124-8{_}1914{_}exclaimed Patsy.
10124-8{_}1915{_}"They're quite liable to dance and murder in the same breath," the Major observed, gloomily.
10124-8{_}1916{_}"I don't like it," said Beth.
10124-8{_}1917{_}"It's something awful just to think of.
10124-8{_}1918{_}Haven't they any gallantry?"
10124-8{_}1919{_}"No," answered Patsy.
10124-8{_}1920{_}"But I wouldn't dance with a lot of half drunken men wearing revolvers, if they burned me at the stake for refusing."
10124-8{_}1921{_}"Ah!
10124-8{_}1922{_}shtick to dat fine expressionment," cried Dan'l, eagerly.
10124-8{_}1923{_}"Shtick to id!
10124-8{_}1924{_}Say you won't dance if dey wear de refolfers--unt den we win de schweepstakes!"
10124-8{_}1925{_}Patsy looked at him critically, in the instant catching a part of his idea.
10124-8{_}1926{_}"What do you mean?"
10124-8{_}1927{_}she asked.
10124-8{_}1928{_}Dan'l explained, while they all listened carefully, absorbed in following in thought his unique suggestions.
10124-8{_}1929{_}"Let's do it!"
10124-8{_}1930{_}exclaimed Beth.
10124-8{_}1931{_}"I'm sure the plan will succeed."
10124-8{_}1932{_}"It's leaving a good deal to chance," objected Uncle John, with a touch of nervousness.
10124-8{_}1933{_}"There is an element of chance in everything," declared Patsy.
10124-8{_}1934{_}"But I'm sure we shall escape, Uncle.
10124-8{_}1935{_}Why it's a regular coup!"
10124-8{_}1936{_}"We take them by surprise, you know," explained the Major, who heartily favored the idea.
10124-8{_}1937{_}They talked it over for a time, perfecting the details, and then became as calm and composed as a group of prisoners might.
10124-8{_}1938{_}Uncle John waved his handkerchief to attract the attention of Wampus, who stole softly around the corner of the house and approached the window, taking care to keep at a respectful distance from the dangerous cactus.
10124-8{_}1939{_}"Is everything ready?"
10124-8{_}1940{_}inquired Uncle John in a subdued voice.
10124-8{_}1941{_}"To be sure all is ready.
10124-8{_}1942{_}Why not?
10124-8{_}1943{_}I am Wampus!"
10124-8{_}1944{_}was the reply, in cautious tones.
10124-8{_}1945{_}"Go back to the machine and guard it carefully, Wampus," commanded Mr. Merrick.
10124-8{_}1946{_}"We expect to escape soon after dark, so have the headlights going, for we shall make a rush for it and there mustn't be a moment's delay."
10124-8{_}1947{_}"All right," said the chauffeur.
10124-8{_}1948{_}"You may depend on me.
10124-8{_}1949{_}I am Wampus, an' not 'fraid of a hundred coward like these.
10124-8{_}1950{_}Is not Mister Algy his eye mos' beautiful blacked?"
10124-8{_}1951{_}"It is," agreed Uncle John.
10124-8{_}1952{_}"Go back to the car now, and wait for us.
10124-8{_}1953{_}Don't get impatient.
10124-8{_}1954{_}We don't know just when we will join you, but it will be as soon as we can manage it.
10124-8{_}1955{_}What is Mumbles doing?"
10124-8{_}1956{_}"Mumble he learn to be good automobilist.
10124-8{_}1957{_}Jus' now he sit on seat an' watch wheel to see nobody touch.
10124-8{_}1958{_}If anybody touch, Mumble he eat him up."
10124-8{_}1959{_}They all laughed at this whimsical notion and it served to relieve the strain of waiting.
10124-8{_}1960{_}Wampus, grinning at the success of his joke, went back to the limousine to inspect it carefully and adjust it in every part until it was in perfect order.
10124-8{_}1961{_}Now that a definite plan of action had been decided upon their spirits rose considerably, and they passed the afternoon in eager anticipation of the crisis.
10124-8{_}1962{_}Rather earlier than expected Stubby and Tim came to say "they had been appointed a committee to escort their guests to the banquet hall, where dinner would at once be served."
10124-8{_}1963{_}"We shall have to clear away for the dance," added Stubby, "so we want to get the feast over with as quickly as possible.
10124-8{_}1964{_}I hope you are all hungry, for Algy has spread himself on this dinner and we are to have every delicacy the ranch affords, regardless of expense.
10124-8{_}1965{_}We can economize afterward to make up for it."
10124-8{_}1966{_}Elaborate preparations were not greatly in evidence, however.
10124-8{_}1967{_}The Mexican servants had washed themselves and the floor of the big room had been swept and cleared of some of its rubbish; but that was all.
10124-8{_}1968{_}The remittance men were in their usual rough costumes and the air was redolent with the fumes of liquor.
10124-8{_}1969{_}CHAPTER XIV  THE ESCAPE   As the prisoners quietly took their places at the table Tobey, who had been drinking hard, decided to make a speech.
10124-8{_}1970{_}His face was badly swollen and he could only see through a slit in one eye, so severe had been the beating administered by Wampus earlier in the day; but the fellow had grit, in spite of his other unmanly qualities, and his imperturbable good humor had scarcely been disturbed by the punishment the Canadian had inflicted upon him.
10124-8{_}1971{_}"Ladies," said he, "and gentlemen--which of course includes our respected male guests--I am happy to inform you that the programme for the First Annual Hades Ranch Ball has finally been arranged, and the dances apportioned in a fair and impartial manner.
10124-8{_}1972{_}The Grand March will take place promptly at seven o'clock, led by Miss Doyle and Knuckles, who has won the privilege by throwing four sixes.
10124-8{_}1973{_}I am to follow with Miss De Graf, and the rest will troop on behind with the privilege of looking at the ladies.
10124-8{_}1974{_}If anyone dares to create disorder his dances with the young ladies will be forfeited.
10124-8{_}1975{_}Dan'l will play the latest dance music on his fiddle, and if it isn't spirited and up-to-date we'll shoot his toes off.
10124-8{_}1976{_}We insist upon plenty of two-steps and waltzes and will wind up with a monney-musk in the gray light of dawn.
10124-8{_}1977{_}This being fully understood, I beg you, my good friends, to fall to and eat and be merry; but don't linger unduly over the dainties, for we are all anxious, like good soldiers, to get into action."
10124-8{_}1978{_}The remittance men applauded this oratory, and incidentally attacked the eatables with evident determination to obey their leader's injunction.
10124-8{_}1979{_}"We can eat any time," remarked Stubby, with his mouth full; "but his Satanic majesty only knows when Hades Ranch will see another dance--with real ladies for partners."
10124-8{_}1980{_}The Chinese cooks and the Mexican servants had a lively time during this meal, for the demands made upon them were incessant.
10124-8{_}1981{_}Uncle John, whose even disposition was seldom ruffled, ate with a good appetite, while even the Major, glum and scowling, did not disdain the numerous well-prepared dishes.
10124-8{_}1982{_}As for Dan'l, he took full advantage of the occasion and was the last one to leave the table.
10124-8{_}1983{_}Our girls, however, were too excited to eat much and little Myrtle, especially, was pallid and uneasy and had a startled look in her eyes whenever anyone made a sudden motion.
10124-8{_}1984{_}As soon as the repast was concluded the servants cleared the long table in a twinkling and pushed it back against the wall at one end of the long room.
10124-8{_}1985{_}A chair was placed for Dan'l on top of this expansive board, which thus became a stage from whence he could overlook the room and the dancers, and then two of the remittance men tossed the old fiddler to his elevated place and commanded him to make ready.
10124-8{_}1986{_}Dan'l said nothing and offered no resistance.
10124-8{_}1987{_}He sat plaintively sawing upon his ancient but rich-toned violin while the floor was brushed, the chairs and benches pushed against the wall and the room prepared for action.
10124-8{_}1988{_}Behind the violinist was a low, broad window facing a grass plot that was free from the terrifying cactus, and the old man noted with satisfaction that it stood wide open.
10124-8{_}1989{_}Uncle John's party had pressed close to the table and stood watching the proceedings.
10124-8{_}1990{_}"Ready now!"
10124-8{_}1991{_}called Tobey; "the Grand March is about to begin.
10124-8{_}1992{_}Take your partners, boys.
10124-8{_}1993{_}Look sharp, there, Dan'l, and give us a martial tune that will lift our feet."
10124-8{_}1994{_}Dan'l meekly set the violin underneath his chin and raised the bow as if in readiness.
10124-8{_}1995{_}"Knuckles," a brawny fellow with a florid face and a peculiar squint, approached Patsy and bowed.
10124-8{_}1996{_}"You're to lead with me, Miss," he said.
10124-8{_}1997{_}"Are you ready?"
10124-8{_}1998{_}"Not quite," she returned with dignified composure; "for I perceive you are not quite ready yourself."
10124-8{_}1999{_}"Eh?
10124-8{_}2000{_}Why not?"
10124-8{_}2001{_}he inquired, surprised.
10124-8{_}2002{_}"You are still wearing your firearms," she replied.
10124-8{_}2003{_}"I cannot and will not dance with a man who carries a revolver."
10124-8{_}2004{_}"That's nothing," he retorted.
10124-8{_}2005{_}"We always do."
10124-8{_}2006{_}"Always?"
10124-8{_}2007{_}"Of course.
10124-8{_}2008{_}And if I shed my gun what's to prevent some one else getting the drop on me?"
10124-8{_}2009{_}"That's it," said Patsy, firmly.
10124-8{_}2010{_}"The weapons must all be surrendered before we begin.
10124-8{_}2011{_}We positively refuse to dance if rioting and shooting are likely to occur."
10124-8{_}2012{_}A murmur of protest arose at this speech, for all the remittance men had gathered around to listen to the argument.
10124-8{_}2013{_}"That's all tommy-rot," observed Handsome Tim, in a sulky tone.
10124-8{_}2014{_}"We're not spoiling for a row; it's the dance we're after."
10124-8{_}2015{_}"Then give up the revolvers," said Beth, coming to her cousin's assistance.
10124-8{_}2016{_}"If this is to be a peaceful entertainment you will not need to be armed, and it is absurd to suppose a lady will dance with a gentleman who is a walking arsenal."
10124-8{_}2017{_}They looked into one another's faces uncertainly.
10124-8{_}2018{_}Dan'l sat softly tuning his violin, as if uninterested in the controversy.
10124-8{_}2019{_}Uncle John and the Major looked on with seeming indifference.
10124-8{_}2020{_}"You must decide which you prefer--the revolvers or the dance," remarked Patsy, staring coolly into the ring of faces.
10124-8{_}2021{_}"Would your English ladies at home consent to dance with armed men?"
10124-8{_}2022{_}asked Beth.
10124-8{_}2023{_}"They're quite right, boys," said Stubby, nodding his bullethead.
10124-8{_}2024{_}"Let's agree to deposit all the shooting irons 'til the dance is over."
10124-8{_}2025{_}"I won't!"
10124-8{_}2026{_}cried Knuckles, his scowl deepening.
10124-8{_}2027{_}"By Jove, you will!"
10124-8{_}2028{_}shouted Tobey, with unexpected vehemence.
10124-8{_}2029{_}"You're delaying the programme, old man, and it's a nuisance to dance in this armor, anyway.
10124-8{_}2030{_}Here--pile all your guns in this corner; every one of you, mind.
10124-8{_}2031{_}Then we shall all stand on an equal footing."
10124-8{_}2032{_}"Put them on the table there, by the old fiddler," said Patsy; "then we will know we are perfectly safe."
10124-8{_}2033{_}Rather unwillingly they complied, each man walking up to the table and placing his revolver at Dan'l's feet.
10124-8{_}2034{_}The girls watched them intently.
10124-8{_}2035{_}"That man over there is still armed," called Beth, pointing to a swarthy Mexican who squatted near the door.
10124-8{_}2036{_}"That's all right," said Tobey, easily.
10124-8{_}2037{_}"He's our guard, Pedro.
10124-8{_}2038{_}I've stationed him there so you won't attempt to escape till we get ready to let you go."
10124-8{_}2039{_}Patsy laughed.
10124-8{_}2040{_}"There's little danger of that," she said.
10124-8{_}2041{_}"All ready, now!"
10124-8{_}2042{_}exclaimed Knuckles, impatiently.
10124-8{_}2043{_}"We're all as harmless as doves.
10124-8{_}2044{_}Let 'er go, Dan'l!"
10124-8{_}2045{_}The old man was just then assisting Uncle John to lift Myrtle to the top of the table, where the Major had placed a chair for her.
10124-8{_}2046{_}Knuckles growled, but waited until the girl was seated near the window.
10124-8{_}2047{_}Then Dan'l drew his bow and struck up a spirited march.
10124-8{_}2048{_}Patsy took the arm of Knuckles and paraded down the long room.
10124-8{_}2049{_}Beth followed with Tobey, and behind them tramped the remittance men in files of two.
10124-8{_}2050{_}At the far end were grouped the servants, looking curiously upon the scene, which was lighted by lamps swung from the ceiling and a row of candles upon the edge of the mantelshelf.
10124-8{_}2051{_}To carry out the idea of a grand march Patsy drew her escort here and there by sharp turns and half circles, the others trailing behind like a huge snake until she had passed down the length of the room and started to return up the other side to the starting point.
10124-8{_}2052{_}So engrossed had been the cowboys that they did not observe the Major and Uncle John clamber upon the table and stand beside Myrtle.
10124-8{_}2053{_}The procession was half way up the hall on its return when Patsy said abruptly: "Now, Beth!"
10124-8{_}2054{_}and darted away from her partner's side and toward the table.
10124-8{_}2055{_}Beth followed like a streak, being an excellent runner, and for a moment Knuckles and Tobey, thus deserted by their partners, stopped to watch them in amazement.
10124-8{_}2056{_}Then their comrades bumped into them and recalled them to their senses.
10124-8{_}2057{_}By that time the two girls had reached the table and leaped upon it.
10124-8{_}2058{_}Uncle John was waving his handkerchief from the window as a signal to Wampus; Dan'l had laid aside his fiddle and seized a revolver in either hand, and the Major had caught up two more of the discarded weapons.
10124-8{_}2059{_}As Beth and Patsy turned, panting, and from their elevation looked up the room, the cowboys gave a bellow of rage and rushed forward.
10124-8{_}2060{_}"Keep back!"
10124-8{_}2061{_}shouted the Major, in stentorian tones, "I'll shoot the first man that interferes."
10124-8{_}2062{_}Noting the grim determination in the old soldier's eye, they hesitated and came to a halt.
10124-8{_}2063{_}"What do you mean by this infernal nonsense?"
10124-8{_}2064{_}cried Tobey, in disgust.
10124-8{_}2065{_}"Why, it's just checkmate, and the game is up," replied Uncle John amiably.
10124-8{_}2066{_}"We've decided not to hold the proposed dance, but to take our departure at once."
10124-8{_}2067{_}He turned and passed Myrtle out of the window where Wampus took her in his arms, crutches and all, and carried her to the automobile.
10124-8{_}2068{_}The remittance men, unarmed and confronted by their own revolvers, stood gaping open-mouthed and seemingly dazed.
10124-8{_}2069{_}"Let's rush 'em, boys!"
10124-8{_}2070{_}shouted Handsome Tim, defiantly.
10124-8{_}2071{_}"Rush 'em alone, if you like," growled Knuckles.
10124-8{_}2072{_}"I'm not ready for the graveyard yet."
10124-8{_}2073{_}"You are vot iss called cowardices," said Dan'l, flourishing the revolvers he held.
10124-8{_}2074{_}"Come on mit der courage, somebotty, so I can shoot holes in you."
10124-8{_}2075{_}"You're building your own coffin just now, Dan'l," retorted Tobey, in baffled rage.
10124-8{_}2076{_}"We know where to get you, old boy, and we'll have revenge for this night's work."
10124-8{_}2077{_}"I vill take some popguns home mit me," was the composed reply.
10124-8{_}2078{_}"Den, ven you come, I vill make a receptioning for you.
10124-8{_}2079{_}Eh?"
10124-8{_}2080{_}Uncle John, Patsy and Beth had followed Myrtle through the window and disappeared.
10124-8{_}2081{_}"Now, sir," said the Major to the old fiddler, "make your escape while I hold them at bay."
10124-8{_}2082{_}"Nod yet," replied Dan'l.
10124-8{_}2083{_}"Ve must gif ourselves de most protectionment ve can."
10124-8{_}2084{_}With this he gathered up the firearms, one by one, and tossed them through the window.
10124-8{_}2085{_}Then he straightened up and a shot flashed down the hall and tumbled the big Mexican guard to the floor just as he was about to glide through the doorway.
10124-8{_}2086{_}"Dit ve say shtand still, or dit ve nod say shtand still?"
10124-8{_}2087{_}asked Dan'l, sternly.
10124-8{_}2088{_}"If somebody gets hurt, it iss because he don'd obey de orderations."
10124-8{_}2089{_}"Go, sir!"
10124-8{_}2090{_}commanded the Major.
10124-8{_}2091{_}"I vill; bud I go last," declared the old man.
10124-8{_}2092{_}"I follow you--see?
10124-8{_}2093{_}Bud you take my violin, please--unt be very tender of id, like id vas your sveetheardt."
10124-8{_}2094{_}The Major took the violin and climbed through the window, proceeding to join the others, who were by now seated in the car.
10124-8{_}2095{_}When he had gone Dan'l prepared to follow, first backing toward the window and then turning to make an agile leap to the ground below.
10124-8{_}2096{_}And now with a shout the cowboys made their rush, only to halt as Dan'l reappeared at the window, covering them again with his revolvers.
10124-8{_}2097{_}"So, you defils--make a listen to me," he called.
10124-8{_}2098{_}"I am experiencing a goot-bye to you, who are jackals unt imitation men unt haf no goot right to be alive.
10124-8{_}2099{_}Also if I see any of you de next time, I vill shoot first unt apologise at der funeral.
10124-8{_}2100{_}I haf no more monkey business mit you voteffer; so keep vere you are until I am gone, unt you vill be safeness."
10124-8{_}2101{_}He slowly backed away from the window, and so thoroughly cowed was the group of ruffians that the old fiddler had been lifted hastily into the automobile before the cowboys mustered courage to leap through the window and search in the darkness for their revolvers, which lay scattered widely upon the ground.
10124-8{_}2102{_}Wampus, chuckling gleefully, jerked the hoods off his glaring searchlights, sprang to his seat and started the machine down the road before the crack of a single revolver was heard in protest.
10124-8{_}2103{_}The shots came thicker after that, but now the automobile was bowling merrily along the road and soon was out of range.
10124-8{_}2104{_}"De road iss exceptionalment goot," remarked Dan'l.
10124-8{_}2105{_}"Dere iss no dangerousness from here to der rifer."
10124-8{_}2106{_}"Danger?"
10124-8{_}2107{_}said the chauffeur, scornfully.
10124-8{_}2108{_}"Who cares for danger?
10124-8{_}2109{_}I am Wampus, an' I am here!"
10124-8{_}2110{_}"We are all here," said Patsy, contentedly nestling against the cushions; "and I'm free to confess that I'm mighty glad of it!"
10124-8{_}2111{_}CHAPTER XV  THE ROMANCE OF DAN'L   It did not take them very long to reach the river, a muddy little stream set below high banks.
10124-8{_}2112{_}By Dan'l's direction they turned to the left and followed the wind of the river for a mile or so until suddenly out of the darkness loomed a quaint little bungalow which the old German claimed to be his home.
10124-8{_}2113{_}"I haf architectured it mineself, unt make it built as I like it.
10124-8{_}2114{_}You vill come in unt shtop der night mit me," he said, as Wampus halted the machine before the door.
10124-8{_}2115{_}There was a little murmur of protest at this, for the house appeared to be scarcely bigger than the automobile.
10124-8{_}2116{_}But Uncle John pointed out, sensibly enough, that they ought not to undertake an unknown road at nighttime, and that Spotville, the town for which they were headed, was still a long way off.
10124-8{_}2117{_}The Major, moreover, had a vivid recollection of his last night's bed upon the roof of the limousine, where he had crept to escape rattlesnakes, and was in no mood to again camp out in the open while they traveled in Arizona.
10124-8{_}2118{_}So he advocated accepting Dan'l's invitation.
10124-8{_}2119{_}The girls, curious to know how so many could be accommodated in the bungalow, withdrew all further objections and stood upon the low, pergola-roofed porch while their host went inside to light the lamps.
10124-8{_}2120{_}They were really surprised at the cosy aspect of the place.
10124-8{_}2121{_}Half the one-story dwelling was devoted to a living room, furnished simply but with modest taste.
10124-8{_}2122{_}A big square table was littered with music, much being in manuscript--thus proving Dan'l's assertion that he was a composer.
10124-8{_}2123{_}Benches were as numerous as chairs, and all were well-cushioned with tanned skins as coverings.
10124-8{_}2124{_}A few good prints were on the walls and the aspect of the place was entirely agreeable to the old man's guests.
10124-8{_}2125{_}As the room was somewhat chilly he made a fire in the ample fireplace and then with an air of pride exhibited to his visitors his tiny kitchen, his own bedroom and a storeroom, which occupied the remainder of the space in the bungalow.
10124-8{_}2126{_}He told them he would prepare beds in the living room for the girls, give his own room to Mr. Merrick and Major Doyle, while he and Wampus would bunk in the storeroom.
10124-8{_}2127{_}"I haf much blankets," he said; "dere vill be no troubles to keep varm."
10124-8{_}2128{_}Afterward they sat before the fire and by the dim lights of the kerosene lamps chatted together of the day's adventures.
10124-8{_}2129{_}Uncle John asked Dan'l what had brought him to this deserted, out-of-the-way spot, and the old man told his story in a manner that amused them all greatly.
10124-8{_}2130{_}"I haf been," said he, "much famous in my time, unt had a individualness pointed out whereeffer I went.
10124-8{_}2131{_}I vas orchestra leader at the Theater Royal in Stuttgart, unt our king haf complimented me many times.
10124-8{_}2132{_}But I vas foolish.
10124-8{_}2133{_}I vas foolish enough to think that ven a man iss great he can stay great.
10124-8{_}2134{_}I married me to a clefer prima donna, unt composed a great opera, which vas finer as anything Herr Wagner has efer done.
10124-8{_}2135{_}Eh?
10124-8{_}2136{_}But dere vas jealousness at work to opposition me.
10124-8{_}2137{_}Von day ven my fine opera vas all complete I vent to the theater to lead mine orchestra.
10124-8{_}2138{_}To my surprisement der Herr Director tells me I can retire on a pension; I am too old unt he has hired a younger man, who iss Herr Gabert.
10124-8{_}2139{_}I go home bewildered unt mishappy, to find that Herr Gabert has stole the score of mine opera unt run avay mit mine vife.
10124-8{_}2140{_}Vot I can do?
10124-8{_}2141{_}Nothing.
10124-8{_}2142{_}Herr Gabert he lead my orchestra tint all der people applauds him.
10124-8{_}2143{_}I am forgot.
10124-8{_}2144{_}One day I see our king compliment Herr Gabert.
10124-8{_}2145{_}He produces my opera unt say he compositioned it.
10124-8{_}2146{_}Eferybody iss crazy aboud id, unt crown Herr Gabert mit flowers.
10124-8{_}2147{_}My vife sings in der opera.
10124-8{_}2148{_}The people cheer her unt she rides avay mit Herr Gabert in his carriage to a grand supper mit der nobility unt der Herr Director.
10124-8{_}2149{_}"I go home unt say: 'Who am I?'
10124-8{_}2150{_}I answer: 'Nobody!'
10124-8{_}2151{_}Am I now great?
10124-8{_}2152{_}No; I am a speck.
10124-8{_}2153{_}Vot can I do?
10124-8{_}2154{_}Veil, I go avay.
10124-8{_}2155{_}I haf some money--a leedle.
10124-8{_}2156{_}I come to America.
10124-8{_}2157{_}I do not like crowds any more.
10124-8{_}2158{_}I like to be alone mit my violin.
10124-8{_}2159{_}I find dis place; I build dis house; I lif here unt make happiness.
10124-8{_}2160{_}My only neighbors are de remittance men, who iss more mischiefing as wicked.
10124-8{_}2161{_}Dey vill nod bother me much.
10124-8{_}2162{_}So after a time I die here.
10124-8{_}2163{_}Vy nod?
10124-8{_}2164{_}I am forgot in Stuttgart."
10124-8{_}2165{_}There was pathos in the tale and his way of telling it.
10124-8{_}2166{_}The old man spoke cheerfully, but they could see before them the tragedy depicted by his simple words.
10124-8{_}2167{_}His hearers were all silent when he had concluded, feeling they could say nothing to console him or lighten his burden.
10124-8{_}2168{_}Only Wampus, sitting in the background, looked scornfully upon the man who had once been the idol of his townspeople.
10124-8{_}2169{_}Dan'l took a violin from a shelf and began to play, softly but with masterly execution.
10124-8{_}2170{_}He caught their mood instantly.
10124-8{_}2171{_}The harmony was restful and contented.
10124-8{_}2172{_}Patsy turned down the lamps, to let the flicker of the firelight dominate the room, and Dan'l understood and blended the flickering light into his melody.
10124-8{_}2173{_}For a long time he continued to improvise, in a way that fairly captivated his hearers, despite their varied temperaments, and made them wonder at his skill.
10124-8{_}2174{_}Then without warning he changed to a stirring, martial air that filled the room with its rich, resonant tones.
10124-8{_}2175{_}There was a fugue, a wonderful finale, and while the concluding notes rang in their ears the old man laid his violin in his lap, leaned back against his cushions and heaved a deep sigh.
10124-8{_}2176{_}They forebore disturbing him for a while.
10124-8{_}2177{_}How strange it seemed that this really talented musician should be banished to a wilderness while still possessing power to stir the souls of men with his marvelous execution.
10124-8{_}2178{_}Truly he was a "maestro," as he had said; a genius whose star had risen, flashed across the sky and suddenly faded, leaving his future a blank.
10124-8{_}2179{_}Wampus moved uneasily in his chair.
10124-8{_}2180{_}"I like to know something," he remarked.
10124-8{_}2181{_}Dan'l roused himself and turned to look at the speaker.
10124-8{_}2182{_}"You have one bad eye," continued Wampus, reflectively.
10124-8{_}2183{_}"What make him so?
10124-8{_}2184{_}You stick violin bow in eye some day?"
10124-8{_}2185{_}"No," grunted Dan'l.
10124-8{_}2186{_}"Bad eye he no make himself," persisted the little chauffeur.
10124-8{_}2187{_}"What make him, then?"
10124-8{_}2188{_}For a moment there was an awkward silence.
10124-8{_}2189{_}The girls considered this personal inquiry offensive and regretted admitting Wampus to the room.
10124-8{_}2190{_}But after a time the old German answered the question, quietly and in a half amused tone.
10124-8{_}2191{_}"Can you nod guess?"
10124-8{_}2192{_}he said.
10124-8{_}2193{_}"Herr Gabert hurt mine eye."
10124-8{_}2194{_}"Oh!"
10124-8{_}2195{_}exclaimed Wampus, nodding approvingly "You fight duel with him?
10124-8{_}2196{_}Of course.
10124-8{_}2197{_}It mus' be."
10124-8{_}2198{_}"I haf one goot eye left, howefer," continued Dan'l.
10124-8{_}2199{_}"It vill do me fery well.
10124-8{_}2200{_}Dere iss nod much to see out here."
10124-8{_}2201{_}"I know," said Wampus.
10124-8{_}2202{_}"But Herr Gabert.
10124-8{_}2203{_}What happen to him?"
10124-8{_}2204{_}Again there was a pause.
10124-8{_}2205{_}Then the German said slowly:  "I am nod rich; but efery year I send a leetle money to Stuttgart to put some flowers on Herr Gabert's grave."
10124-8{_}2206{_}The chauffeur's face brightened.
10124-8{_}2207{_}He got up from his chair and solemnly shook Dan'l's hand.
10124-8{_}2208{_}"You are great musician," he announced.
10124-8{_}2209{_}"You can believe it, for it is true.
10124-8{_}2210{_}An' you have shake the hand of great chauffeur.
10124-8{_}2211{_}I am Wampus."
10124-8{_}2212{_}Dan'l did not answer.
10124-8{_}2213{_}He had covered his good eye with his hand.
10124-8{_}2214{_}CHAPTER XVI  THE LODGING AT SPOTVILLE   "Wake up, Patsy: I smell coffee!"
10124-8{_}2215{_}called Beth, and soon the two girls were dressed and assisting Myrtle to complete her toilet.
10124-8{_}2216{_}Through the open windows came the cool, fragrant breath of morning; the sky was beginning to blush at the coming of the sun.
10124-8{_}2217{_}"To think of our getting up at such unearthly hours!"
10124-8{_}2218{_}cried Patsy cheerfully.
10124-8{_}2219{_}"But I don't mind it in the least, Beth; do you?"
10124-8{_}2220{_}"I love the daybreak," returned Beth, softly.
10124-8{_}2221{_}"We've wasted the best hours of morning abed, Patsy, these many years."
10124-8{_}2222{_}"But there's a difference," said Myrtle, earnestly.
10124-8{_}2223{_}"I know the daybreak in the city very well, for nearly all my life I have had to rise in the dark in order to get my breakfast and be at work on time.
10124-8{_}2224{_}It is different from this, I assure you; especially in winter, when the chill strikes through to your bones.
10124-8{_}2225{_}Even in summer time the air of the city is overheated and close, and the early mornings cheerless and uncomfortable.
10124-8{_}2226{_}Then I think it is best to stay in bed as long as you can--if you have nothing else to do.
10124-8{_}2227{_}But here, out in the open, it seems a shame not to be up with the birds to breathe the scent of the fields and watch the sun send his heralds ahead of him to proclaim his coming and then climb from the bottomless pit into the sky and take possession of it."
10124-8{_}2228{_}"Why, Myrtle!"
10124-8{_}2229{_}exclaimed Patsy, wonderingly; "what a poetic notion.
10124-8{_}2230{_}How did it get into your head, little one?"
10124-8{_}2231{_}Myrtle's sweet face rivaled the sunrise for a moment.
10124-8{_}2232{_}She made no reply but only smiled pathetically.
10124-8{_}2233{_}Uncle John's knock upon the door found them ready for breakfast, which old Dan'l had skilfully prepared in the tiny kitchen and now placed upon a round table set out upon the porch.
10124-8{_}2234{_}By the time they had finished the simple meal Wampus had had his coffee and prepared the automobile for the day's journey.
10124-8{_}2235{_}A few minutes later they said good-bye to the aged musician and took the trail that led through Spotville.
10124-8{_}2236{_}The day's trip was without event.
10124-8{_}2237{_}They encountered one or two Indians on the way, jogging slowly along on their shaggy ponies; but the creatures were mild and inoffensive.
10124-8{_}2238{_}The road was fairly good and they made excellent time, so that long before twilight Spotville was reached and the party had taken possession of the one small and primitive "hotel" the place afforded.
10124-8{_}2239{_}It was a two-story, clapboarded building, the lower floor being devoted to the bar and dining room, while the second story was divided into box-like bedrooms none too clean and very cheaply furnished.
10124-8{_}2240{_}"I imagine we shall find this place 'the limit'," remarked Uncle John ruefully.
10124-8{_}2241{_}"But surely we shall be able to stand it for one night," he added, with a philosophic sigh.
10124-8{_}2242{_}"Want meat fer supper?"
10124-8{_}2243{_}asked the landlord, a tall, gaunt man who considered himself dressed when he was in his shirt sleeves.
10124-8{_}2244{_}"What kind of meat?"
10124-8{_}2245{_}inquired Uncle John, cautiously.
10124-8{_}2246{_}"Kin give yeh fried pork er jerked beef.
10124-8{_}2247{_}Ham 'a all out an' the chickens is beginnin' to lay."
10124-8{_}2248{_}"Eggs?"
10124-8{_}2249{_}"Of course, stranger.
10124-8{_}2250{_}Thet's the on'y thing Spotville chickens lay, nowadays.
10124-8{_}2251{_}I s'pose whar yeh come from they lay biscuits 'n' pork chops."
10124-8{_}2252{_}"No.
10124-8{_}2253{_}Door knobs, sometimes," said Mr. Merrick, "but seldom pork chops.
10124-8{_}2254{_}Let's have eggs, and perhaps a little fried pork to go with them.
10124-8{_}2255{_}Any milk?"
10124-8{_}2256{_}"Canned er fresh?"
10124-8{_}2257{_}"Fresh preferred."
10124-8{_}2258{_}The landlord looked at him steadily.
10124-8{_}2259{_}"Yeh've come a long-way, stranger," he said, "an' yeh must 'a' spent a lot of money, here 'n' there.
10124-8{_}2260{_}Air yeh prepared to pay fer thet order in solid cash?"
10124-8{_}2261{_}Uncle John seemed startled, and looked at the Major, who smiled delightedly.
10124-8{_}2262{_}"Are such things expensive, sir?"
10124-8{_}2263{_}the latter asked the landlord.
10124-8{_}2264{_}"Why, we don't eat 'em ourselves, 'n' thet's a cold fact.
10124-8{_}2265{_}Eggs is eggs, an' brings forty cents a dozen to ship.
10124-8{_}2266{_}There's seven cows in town, 'n' forty-one babies, so yeh kin figger what fresh milk's worth."
10124-8{_}2267{_}"Perhaps," said Uncle John mildly, "we can stand the expense--if we won't rob the babies."
10124-8{_}2268{_}"Don't worry 'bout thet.
10124-8{_}2269{_}The last autymobble folks as come this way got hot because I charged 'em market prices fer the truck they et.
10124-8{_}2270{_}So I'm jest inquirin' beforehand, to save hard feelin's.
10124-8{_}2271{_}I've found out one thing 'bout autymobble folks sense I've ben runnin' this hoe-tel, an' thet is thet a good many is ownin' machines thet oughter be payin' their bills instid o' buyin' gasoline."
10124-8{_}2272{_}The Major took him aside.
10124-8{_}2273{_}He did not tell the cautious landlord that Mr. Merrick was one of the wealthiest men in America, but he exhibited a roll of bills that satisfied the man his demands would be paid in full.
10124-8{_}2274{_}The touring; party feasted upon eggs and fresh milk, both very delicious but accompanied by odds and ends of food not so palatable.
10124-8{_}2275{_}The landlord's two daughters, sallow, sunken cheeked girls, waited on the guests and the landlord's wife did the cooking.
10124-8{_}2276{_}Beth, Patsy and Myrtle retired early, as did Uncle John.
10124-8{_}2277{_}The Major, smoking his "bedtime cigar," as he called it, strolled out into the yard and saw Wampus seated in the automobile, also smoking.
10124-8{_}2278{_}"We get an early start to-morrow, Wampus," said the Major.
10124-8{_}2279{_}"Better get to bed."
10124-8{_}2280{_}"Here is my bed," returned the chauffeur, quietly.
10124-8{_}2281{_}"But there's a room reserved for you in the hotel."
10124-8{_}2282{_}"I know.
10124-8{_}2283{_}Don't want him.
10124-8{_}2284{_}I sleep me here."
10124-8{_}2285{_}The Major looked at him reflectively.
10124-8{_}2286{_}"Ever been in this town before, Wampus?"
10124-8{_}2287{_}he asked.
10124-8{_}2288{_}"No, sir.
10124-8{_}2289{_}But I been in other towns like him, an' know this kind of hotel.
10124-8{_}2290{_}Then why do I sleep in front seat of motor car?"
10124-8{_}2291{_}"Because you are foolish, I suppose, being born that way and unable to escape your heritage.
10124-8{_}2292{_}For my part, I shall sleep in a bed; like a Christian," said the Major rather testily.
10124-8{_}2293{_}"Even Christian cannot sleep sometime," returned Wampus, leaning back in his seat and puffing a cloud of smoke into the clear night air.
10124-8{_}2294{_}"For me, I am good Christian; but I am not martyr."
10124-8{_}2295{_}"What do you mean by that?"
10124-8{_}2296{_}demanded the Major.
10124-8{_}2297{_}"Do you sometime gamble?"
10124-8{_}2298{_}inquired Wampus softly.
10124-8{_}2299{_}"Not often, sir."
10124-8{_}2300{_}"But sometime?
10124-8{_}2301{_}Ah!
10124-8{_}2302{_}Then I make you a bet.
10124-8{_}2303{_}I bet you ten dollar to one cent you not sleep in your bed to-night."
10124-8{_}2304{_}The Major coughed.
10124-8{_}2305{_}Then he frowned.
10124-8{_}2306{_}"Is it so bad as that?"
10124-8{_}2307{_}he asked.
10124-8{_}2308{_}"I think he is."
10124-8{_}2309{_}"I'll not believe it!"
10124-8{_}2310{_}exclaimed Major Doyle.
10124-8{_}2311{_}"This hotel isn't what you might call first-class, and can't rank with the Waldorf-Astoria; but I imagine the beds will be very comfortable."
10124-8{_}2312{_}"Once," said Wampus, "I have imagination, too.
10124-8{_}2313{_}Now I have experience; so I sleep in automobile."
10124-8{_}2314{_}The Major walked away with an exclamation of impatience.
10124-8{_}2315{_}He had never possessed much confidence in the Canadian's judgment and on this occasion he considered the fellow little wiser than a fool.
10124-8{_}2316{_}Wampus rolled himself in a rug and was about to stretch his moderate length upon the broad double seat when a pattering of footsteps was heard and Beth came up to the car.
10124-8{_}2317{_}She was wrapped in a dark cloak and carried a bundle of clothing under one arm and her satchel in the unoccupied hand.
10124-8{_}2318{_}There was a new moon which dimly lighted the scene, but as all the townspeople were now in bed and the hotel yard deserted there was no one to remark upon the girl's appearance.
10124-8{_}2319{_}"Wampus," she said, "let me into the limousine, please.
10124-8{_}2320{_}The night is so perfect I've decided to sleep here in the car."
10124-8{_}2321{_}The chauffeur jumped down and opened the door.
10124-8{_}2322{_}"One moment an' I make up the beds for all," he said.
10124-8{_}2323{_}"Never mind that," Beth answered.
10124-8{_}2324{_}"The others are all asleep, I'm sure."
10124-8{_}2325{_}Wampus shook his head.
10124-8{_}2326{_}"They all be here pretty soon," he predicted, and proceeded to deftly prepare the interior of the limousine for the expected party.
10124-8{_}2327{_}When Beth had entered the car Wampus pitched the lean-to tent and arranged the cots as he was accustomed to do when they "camped out."
10124-8{_}2328{_}Scarcely had he completed this task when Patsy and Myrtle appeared.
10124-8{_}2329{_}They began to explain their presence, but Wampus interrupted them, saying:  "All right, Miss Patsy an' Miss Myrtle.
10124-8{_}2330{_}Your beds he made up an' Miss 'Lizbeth already asleep in him."
10124-8{_}2331{_}So they crept inside with sighs of relief, and Wampus had just mounted to the front seat again and disposed himself to rest when Uncle John trotted up, clad in his trousers and shirt, with the balance of his apparel clasped in his arms.
10124-8{_}2332{_}He looked at the tent with pleased approval.
10124-8{_}2333{_}"Good boy, Wampus!"
10124-8{_}2334{_}he exclaimed.
10124-8{_}2335{_}"That room they gave me is an inferno.
10124-8{_}2336{_}I'm afraid our young ladies won't sleep a wink."
10124-8{_}2337{_}"Oh, yes," returned Wampus with a nod; "all three now inside car, safe an' happy."
10124-8{_}2338{_}"I'm glad of it.
10124-8{_}2339{_}How was your own room, Wampus?"
10124-8{_}2340{_}"I have not seen him, sir.
10124-8{_}2341{_}But I have suspect him; so I sleep here."
10124-8{_}2342{_}"You are a wise chauffeur--a rare genus, in other words.
10124-8{_}2343{_}Good night, Wampus.
10124-8{_}2344{_}Where's the Major?"
10124-8{_}2345{_}Wampus chuckled.
10124-8{_}2346{_}"In hotel.
10124-8{_}2347{_}Sir, do the Major swear sometime?"
10124-8{_}2348{_}Uncle John crept under the tent.
10124-8{_}2349{_}"If he does," he responded, "he's swearing this blessed minute.
10124-8{_}2350{_}Anyhow, I'll guarantee he's not asleep."
10124-8{_}2351{_}Wampus again mounted to his perch.
10124-8{_}2352{_}"No use my try to sleep 'til Major he come," he muttered, and settled himself to wait.
10124-8{_}2353{_}It was not long.
10124-8{_}2354{_}Presently some one approached on a run, and a broad grin overspread the chauffeur's features.
10124-8{_}2355{_}The Major had not delayed his escape long enough to don his trousers even; he had grabbed his belongings in both arms and fled in his blue and white striped undergarments.
10124-8{_}2356{_}Wampus leaped down and lifted the flap of the tent.
10124-8{_}2357{_}The Major paused long enough in the moonlight to stare at the chauffeur and say sternly:  "If you utter one syllable, you rascal, I'll punch your head!"
10124-8{_}2358{_}Wampus was discreet.
10124-8{_}2359{_}He said not a word.
10124-8{_}2360{_}CHAPTER XVII  YELLOW POPPIES   "So this is California!"
10124-8{_}2361{_}exclaimed Patsy gleefully, as the automobile left Parker and crossed the Arizona line.
10124-8{_}2362{_}"But it doesn't look any different," said Myrtle, peering out of the window.
10124-8{_}2363{_}"Of course not," observed Uncle John.
10124-8{_}2364{_}"A State boundary is a man-made thing, and doesn't affect the country a bit.
10124-8{_}2365{_}We've just climbed a miniature mountain back in Arizona, and now we must climb a mate to it in California.
10124-8{_}2366{_}But the fact is, we've entered at last the Land of Enchantment, and every mile now will bring us nearer and nearer to the roses and sunshine."
10124-8{_}2367{_}"There's sunshine here now," declared the Major.
10124-8{_}2368{_}"We've had it right along.
10124-8{_}2369{_}But I haven't seen the roses yet, and a pair of ear muffs wouldn't be uncomfortable in this cutting breeze."
10124-8{_}2370{_}"The air _is_ rather crisp," admitted Uncle John.
10124-8{_}2371{_}"But we're still in the mountainous district, and Haggerty says--"  The Major coughed derisively and Mumbles barked and looked at Uncle John sagaciously.
10124-8{_}2372{_}"Haggerty says--"  "Is that a rabbit or a squirrel?
10124-8{_}2373{_}Something has caught the eye of our Mumbles," interrupted the Major, pointing vaguely across the mesa.
10124-8{_}2374{_}"Haggerty says--"  "I wonder if Mumbles could catch 'em," remarked the Major, with complacence.
10124-8{_}2375{_}"He says that every mile we travel brings us nearer the scent of the orange blossoms and the glare of the yellow poppies," persisted Uncle John.
10124-8{_}2376{_}"You see, we've taken the Southern route, after all, for soon we shall be on the Imperial road, which leads to San Diego--in the heart of the gorgeous Southland."
10124-8{_}2377{_}"What is the Imperial road?"
10124-8{_}2378{_}inquired Beth.
10124-8{_}2379{_}"The turnpike through Imperial Valley, said to be the richest bit of land in all the world, not excepting the famous Nile banks of Egypt.
10124-8{_}2380{_}There is no railway there yet, but the Valley is settling very fast, and Haggerty says--"  "How remarkable!"
10124-8{_}2381{_}exclaimed the Major, gazing straight ahead.
10124-8{_}2382{_}And again Mumbles, curled in Patsy's lap, lifted his shaggy head and gave a wailing bark.
10124-8{_}2383{_}Uncle John frowned, but was loyal to Haggerty.
10124-8{_}2384{_}"He says that if America was now unknown to all the countries of the world, Imperial would soon make it famous.
10124-8{_}2385{_}They grow wonderful crops there--strawberries and melons the year around, as well as all the tropical and semi-tropical fruits and grains, flowers and vines known to any country yet discovered."
10124-8{_}2386{_}"Do we go to Imperial?"
10124-8{_}2387{_}asked Myrtle, eagerly.
10124-8{_}2388{_}"I think not, my dear; we just skirt the edge of the Valley.
10124-8{_}2389{_}It's rather wild and primitive there yet; for although many settlers are flocking to that favored district Imperial is large enough to be an empire by itself.
10124-8{_}2390{_}However, we shall find an ideal climate at Coronado, by the edge of the blue Pacific, and there and at Los Angeles we shall rest from our journey and get acquainted with the wonders of the Golden State.
10124-8{_}2391{_}Has the trip tired you, girls?"
10124-8{_}2392{_}"Not me," answered Beth, promptly.
10124-8{_}2393{_}"I've enjoyed every mile of the way."
10124-8{_}2394{_}"And so have I," added Patsy; "except perhaps the adventure with the remittance men.
10124-8{_}2395{_}But I wouldn't care to have missed even that, for it led to our acquaintance with old Dan'l."
10124-8{_}2396{_}"For my part," said Myrtle softly, "I've been in a real fairyland.
10124-8{_}2397{_}It has seemed like a dream to me, all this glorious journey, and I shall hate to wake up, as I must in time."
10124-8{_}2398{_}"Don't worry just yet about the awakening, dear," returned Patsy, leaning over to kiss her little friend.
10124-8{_}2399{_}"Just enjoy it while you can.
10124-8{_}2400{_}If fairylands exist, they were made for just such as you, Myrtle."
10124-8{_}2401{_}"One of the greatest marvels of our trip," said the Major, with a smile, "is the improvement in our dear little invalid.
10124-8{_}2402{_}It isn't the same Myrtle who started out with us, believe me.
10124-8{_}2403{_}Can't you all see the change?"
10124-8{_}2404{_}"I can _feel_ it," returned Myrtle, happily.
10124-8{_}2405{_}"And don't you notice how well I walk, and how little use I have now for the crutches?"
10124-8{_}2406{_}"And can you feel the rosy cheeks and bright eyes, too?"
10124-8{_}2407{_}asked Uncle John, regarding her with much satisfaction.
10124-8{_}2408{_}"The trip was just the thing for Myrtle," added Patsy.
10124-8{_}2409{_}"She has grown stronger every day; but she is not quite well yet, you know, and I depend a good deal upon the genial climate of California to insure her complete recovery."
10124-8{_}2410{_}Uncle John did not reply.
10124-8{_}2411{_}He remembered the doctor's assertion that a painful operation would be necessary to finally restore Myrtle to a normal condition, and his kindly heart disliked to reflect upon the ordeal before the poor girl.
10124-8{_}2412{_}Haggerty proved a prophet, after all.
10124-8{_}2413{_}Each mile they covered opened new vistas of delight to the eager travelers.
10124-8{_}2414{_}The air grew more balmy as they left the high altitudes and came upon the level country to the north, of the San Bernardino range of mountains, nor was it long before they sighted Imperial and sped through miles of country carpeted with the splendid yellow poppies which the State has adopted as the emblems of California.
10124-8{_}2415{_}And behind this golden robe loomed the cotton fields of Imperial, one of the most fascinating sights the traveler may encounter.
10124-8{_}2416{_}They made a curve to the right here, and headed northerly until they came to Salton.
10124-8{_}2417{_}Skirting the edge of the curious Salton Sea they now headed directly west toward Escondido, finding the roads remarkably good and for long stretches as smooth and hard as an asphalt boulevard.
10124-8{_}2418{_}The three days it took them to cross the State were days of wonder and delight.
10124-8{_}2419{_}It was not long before they encountered the roses and carnations growing on every side, which the Major had persistently declared to be mythical.
10124-8{_}2420{_}"It seems all wrong," asserted Patsy's father, moodily, "for such delicate flowers to be growing out of doors in midwinter.
10124-8{_}2421{_}And look at the grass!
10124-8{_}2422{_}Why, the seasons are changed about.
10124-8{_}2423{_}It's Springtime just now in California."
10124-8{_}2424{_}"The man at the last stop we made told me his roses bloomed the year round," said Patsy, "And just smell the orange blossoms, will you!
10124-8{_}2425{_}Aren't they sweet, and don't they remind you of brides?"
10124-8{_}2426{_}From Escondido it was a short run to the sea and their first glimpse of the majestic Pacific was from a high bluff overhanging the water.
10124-8{_}2427{_}From this point the road ran south to San Diego, skirting the coast along a mountain trail that is admitted to be one of the most picturesque rides in America.
10124-8{_}2428{_}Descending the hills as they neared San Diego they passed through fields of splendid wild flowers so extensive and beautiful that our girls fairly gasped in wonder.
10124-8{_}2429{_}The yellow and orange poppies predominated, but there were acres of wild mustard throwing countless numbers of gorgeous saffron spikes skyward, and vistas of blue carconnes, white daisies and blood-red delandres.
10124-8{_}2430{_}The yucca was in bloom, too, and added its mammoth flower to the display.
10124-8{_}2431{_}They did not halt at San Diego, the southernmost city of California, from whence the Mexican line is in plain sight, but drove to the bay, where Wampus guided the limousine on to the big ferryboat bound for Coronado.
10124-8{_}2432{_}They all left the car during the brief voyage and watched the porpoises sporting in the clear water of the bay and gazed abstractedly at the waving palms on the opposite shore, where lies nestled "the Crown of the Pacific"--Coronado.
10124-8{_}2433{_}CHAPTER XVIII  THE SILENT MAN   Even the Major smiled benignantly when he reached his appointed room in the magnificent Hotel del Coronado, which is famed throughout the world.
10124-8{_}2434{_}"This," said he, "reminds me of New York; and it's the first thing that has, since I left home."
10124-8{_}2435{_}"Why, Daddy, it isn't like New York at all," protested Patsy, standing beside him at the broad window overlooking the ocean.
10124-8{_}2436{_}"Did you ever see a palm tree waving in New York; or daisy bushes as tall as a man; or such masses of roses and flowering vines?
10124-8{_}2437{_}And then just notice the mountains over there--they're in Mexico, I'm told--and this great headland in the other direction; it's called Point Loma.
10124-8{_}2438{_}Oh, I never imagined any place could be so beautiful!"
10124-8{_}2439{_}The others were equally excited, and Uncle John said, smiling broadly:  "Well, we're here at last, my dears, and I'm sure we are already well paid for our trip across the continent.
10124-8{_}2440{_}What pleasant rooms these are.
10124-8{_}2441{_}If the hotel table is at all to be compared with the house itself we shall have a happy time here, which means we will stay as long as possible."
10124-8{_}2442{_}But the table was another surprise, for the meals were equal to any served in the great Eastern metropolis.
10124-8{_}2443{_}Uncle John complimented the landlord, a cheery faced, fat little man who had at one time managed a famous New York hotel and had brought his talents and experience to far California.
10124-8{_}2444{_}"I'm sorry," said this gentle boniface, "that I could not reserve better rooms for you--for there are some choice views from some locations.
10124-8{_}2445{_}I had a corner suite saved for your party, a suite I consider the most desirable in the hotel; but an eccentric individual arrived yesterday who demanded the entire suite, and I had to let him have it.
10124-8{_}2446{_}He will not stay long, and as soon as he goes you shall have the rooms."
10124-8{_}2447{_}"Who is he?"
10124-8{_}2448{_}asked Uncle John.
10124-8{_}2449{_}"A rich miner; a most melancholy and peculiar person, by the way," replied landlord Ross.
10124-8{_}2450{_}"I believe his name is Jones."
10124-8{_}2451{_}Mr. Merrick started.
10124-8{_}2452{_}"Jones, and a miner?"
10124-8{_}2453{_}he said.
10124-8{_}2454{_}"What's his other name--Anson?"
10124-8{_}2455{_}"We'll look and see," replied Mr. Ross, turning to the hotel register.
10124-8{_}2456{_}"No; not Anson.
10124-8{_}2457{_}He is registered as C.B.
10124-8{_}2458{_}Jones, of Boston."
10124-8{_}2459{_}"Oh; that's not the Jones at all," said Uncle John, disappointed.
10124-8{_}2460{_}"It's the Jones who is our guest," replied the landlord, smiling.
10124-8{_}2461{_}Meantime the three girls had gone for a walk along the coast.
10124-8{_}2462{_}The beach is beautiful at Coronado.
10124-8{_}2463{_}There is a high sea wall of rock, and the path runs along its edge almost the length of the promontory.
10124-8{_}2464{_}The rocks are sloping, however, and it is not very difficult to climb down them to where the waves break against the wall.
10124-8{_}2465{_}Near the hotel they met straggling groups, strolling in either direction, but half a mile away the promenade was practically deserted.
10124-8{_}2466{_}It was beginning to grow dark, and Beth said, regretfully:  "We must get back, girls, and dress for dinner--an unusual luxury, isn't it?
10124-8{_}2467{_}Our trunks arrived at the hotel two weeks ago, and are now in our rooms, doubtless, awaiting us to unpack them."
10124-8{_}2468{_}"Don't let's return just yet," begged Myrtle.
10124-8{_}2469{_}"I want to see the sun set."
10124-8{_}2470{_}"It will be gorgeous," said Patsy, glancing at the sky; "but we can see it from our windows, and as we're a long way from the hotel now I believe Beth's suggestion is wise."
10124-8{_}2471{_}So they began to retrace their steps.
10124-8{_}2472{_}Myrtle still walked with some difficulty, and they had not proceeded far when Beth exclaimed:  "Look at that man down there!"
10124-8{_}2473{_}Her companions followed her direction and saw standing upon a huge pile of rocks at the water's edge a slight, solitary figure.
10124-8{_}2474{_}Something in the poise, as he leaned forward staring at the darkened waves--for the sun was low and cast shadows aslant the water--struck Myrtle as familiar.
10124-8{_}2475{_}"Oh, girls!"
10124-8{_}2476{_}she exclaimed; "it's the Grand Canyon man."
10124-8{_}2477{_}"Why, I believe it is," agreed Patsy.
10124-8{_}2478{_}"What is he doing?"
10124-8{_}2479{_}"Nothing," said Beth, briefly.
10124-8{_}2480{_}"But he is going to do something, I think."
10124-8{_}2481{_}While they stared at him from their elevation the man straightened an instant and cast a hasty glance to either side.
10124-8{_}2482{_}The place seemed to him deserted, for he failed to observe the group of three intently watching his motions from the high bank overhead.
10124-8{_}2483{_}Next moment he turned back to the water and leaned over the edge of rock again.
10124-8{_}2484{_}"Don't!"
10124-8{_}2485{_}cried Myrtle, her clear voice ringing over the lap of the waves; "please don't!"
10124-8{_}2486{_}He swung around and turned his gaunt features upward to where the young girl leaned upon her crutches, with clasped hands and a look of distress upon her sweet face.
10124-8{_}2487{_}"Don't!"
10124-8{_}2488{_}she repeated, pleadingly.
10124-8{_}2489{_}He passed his hand over his eyes with a very weary gesture and looked at Myrtle again--this time quite steadily.
10124-8{_}2490{_}She was trembling in every limb and her cheeks were white with fear.
10124-8{_}2491{_}Slowly--very slowly--the man turned and began to climb the rocks; not directly upward to where the girls stood, but diagonally, so as to reach the walk some distance ahead of them.
10124-8{_}2492{_}They did not move until he had gained the path and turned toward the hotel.
10124-8{_}2493{_}Then they followed and kept him in sight until he reached the entrance to the court and disappeared within.
10124-8{_}2494{_}"I wonder," said Patsy, as they made their way to their rooms, "whether he really was thinking of plunging into the ocean; or whether that time at the Grand Canyon he had a notion of jumping into the chasm."
10124-8{_}2495{_}"If so," added Beth, "Myrtle has saved his life twice.
10124-8{_}2496{_}But she can't be always near to watch the man, and if he has suicidal intentions, he'll make an end of himself, sooner or later, without a doubt."
